## privacy & security

- [ ] **[HIGH PRIORITY — SECURITY] Privacy gate before every public-remote push — globally** — this repo is PUBLIC; personal identity strings can slip in via docs/scripts. Build a **pre-push privacy gate that runs globally** (every repo, before any push to a PUBLIC remote): a `pre-push` git hook installed via global `core.hooksPath` (or wired into `git-diary-workflow/git-lock-push.sh` before the `git push`) that scans the about-to-be-pushed **diff** for leak patterns and BLOCKS (loud, overridable) when the remote host is public (e.g. a public forge) — lenient/skip for private remotes. Pattern classes: emails, home-dir absolute paths, machine hostnames, real-name strings, `accessToken`/`api[_-]?key`/`-----BEGIN`/`password=` secrets, session UUIDs. Must be **allowlist-aware** (some matches are intentional/functional) and scan the diff/new content (not the whole tree) so it isn't noisy. Pair with a global `~/.claude/CLAUDE.md` rule. Mechanism lives in `dotclaude-skills/hooks/` + installed globally. **NOTE — keep specifics OUT of this public file:** a 2026-06-19 scan found concrete leak vectors (and confirmed NO hardcoded secrets); the detailed findings + triage targets are recorded in **private session memory** (`privacy-scan-findings-2026-06-19`), not here, because enumerating them in the published repo amplifies the leak. One finding is behavioural (a functional author-name match that must be externalized, not deleted); the rest are scrub/aliasing decisions. **Concrete motivating instance (2026-06-30):** a session committed portfolio-specific terms into this public TODO while *filing privacy items*, with no leak check — exactly what this gate would block (details in private memory). **RECONCILED 2026-07-19 (meeting `docs/meeting-notes/2026-07-19-1212-git-hook-enforcement-substrate-reconciliation.md`):** the git-hook install infra this item named (`core.hooksPath`) is now the shared **id:7a05 framework** — build the framework ONCE there; ebd0 = the privacy **pre-push** check registering into it. — **DECIDED 2026-07-20 (meeting `docs/meeting-notes/2026-07-20-1241-privacy-gate-pre-push-ebd0.md`, D1–D4):** ship a STANDALONE `hooks/pre-push-privacy-gate.sh` NOW (global `core.hooksPath`, same surface 7a05 will later adopt — NOT gated on 7a05); engine = bespoke fleet-specific pattern set + best-effort `scan_pii()` shell-out (no hard cross-repo import); **warn+LOG mode first** (exit 0, never auto-block — build the logger, calibrate FP), flip to block-with-override via id:df87; patterns+allowlist in a NEW PRIVATE `~/.config/` file (id:7fff) — public repo ships mechanism + a generic `~/.claude/CLAUDE.md` rule only. — **BUILD SHIPPED (item stays OPEN until ACTIVE — tick-on-active invariant, chidiai case 2026-07-20-relay-integrator-ticked-high-priority-security) 2026-07-20 (execute[opus]+review SHIP):** hooks/pre-push-privacy-gate.sh (warn+LOG, D1-D4) + test + `make install-privacy-gate` target shipped, suite 276/0. **The gate is INERT until ACTIVATED** — activation = populate the private pattern file (id:7fff, hands) + run `make install-privacy-gate` to set global core.hooksPath (hands) + later warn→block flip (id:df87). Buildable core complete; activation tracked by id:7fff/df87. <!-- id:ebd0 -->

## documentation

- [ ] **Global glossary — project names, coined keywords, and project aliases (single source, PRIVATE)** (user 2026-06-30) — maintain one glossary that defines (1) **project names** across the `~/src` portfolio, (2) **coined keywords/terms** the user uses that aren't self-evident — a "term → defining project/note" lookup so an agent can resolve a coined term deterministically instead of guessing or asking (the motivating example that triggered this item, and its resolution, are kept in **private session memory** — not enumerated in this public file, per the privacy note below), and (3) **project aliases** (e.g. `.mw` → `mathematical-writing`) which **already partly live in `relay.toml`**. Purpose: an agent (or human) can resolve an alias/keyword deterministically instead of guessing or asking. **PRIVACY — load-bearing (cf. [[feedback-no-leak-specifics-in-public-files]], privacy-scan id:ebd0):** `dotclaude-skills` is a PUBLIC repo, and an enumerated list of project names + aliases IS the *project-portfolio* leak vector the 2026-06-19 scan flagged — so the glossary **CONTENT must live in a PRIVATE location, never committed here**. `relay.toml` (`~/.config/relay/`, local-only/untracked) is the right model and likely substrate: it already holds the own-repo set, `# path:` overrides, and aliases, so **extend it (or a sibling private file it points to) rather than duplicate** (cf. [[feedback-use-existing-tools-not-improvise]] — relay.toml is THE registry; don't re-derive). The public repo gets at most a generic *mechanism* (alias/keyword resolver that reads the private source) + a pointer. **Consumers:** relay (`# path:`/alias resolution already), `/meeting`, project_manager `proj` (knows all projects), and agent term-resolution. Design Qs for a `[HARD — meeting]`: exact home + schema (relay.toml `[aliases]`/`[glossary]` table vs sibling file), keyword vs name vs alias namespacing, and whether it's hand-maintained or partly derived from relay.toml + project scan. <!-- id:2a3d -->

## locks & concurrency

- [ ] **[HIGH PRIORITY] Lock hygiene umbrella — prevent avoidable locks, auto-recover the unavoidable ones** — across the relay/git toolchain, lock-related stalls keep costing manual intervention. Two goals: **(A) PREVENT avoidable locks** and **(B) AUTO-FIX/AUTO-RECOVER** the rest so a human never has to `rm` a lock or hand-clean a tree. Known lock surfaces to cover: (1) stale `.git/index.lock` left by a killed/OOM'd git process (cf. [[oom-local-model-session-kills]] — 6 sessions died at once) → blocks every subsequent git op until manually removed; a pre-op guard should detect a lock whose owning PID is dead (or older than a TTL) and clear it before retrying. (2) flock files — `.git-lock-push.lock`, `/tmp/claude-git-*.lock`, broker/append locks — the 30s flock timeout fails the op rather than diagnosing a dead holder; add PID-liveness + stale-age recovery and a clear error naming the holder. (3) the **fd-8 self-nesting deadlock** in `git-lock-push.sh` (a caller already holding the repo lock re-execs `8>` the same file → 30s deadlock) — id:3b18. (4) `claim.sh` leases that outlive a dead run (already TTL-expire, but verify no path leaves a permanent lease). (5) dirty-tree "soft locks" that block dispatch/integration: build-artifact false-positives (id:6366), `uv.lock` drift (id:bae5), orphan worktrees from un-`--force`d removal (id:d187). The deeper structural fix for write contention is worktree-per-session + flock'd merge (id:3558). **This item is the umbrella**: triage which lock surfaces are *avoidable by design* (eliminate) vs *need auto-recovery* (build a shared stale-lock reaper: PID-liveness + mtime-TTL, used by git-diary-workflow, relay integrator, append.sh, broker), then either close via the existing point-items or spawn new ones. Observe-before-preventing applies (cf. design heuristics) — but the manual-cost evidence already exists across the cited ids. Trigger: 2026-06-21 `/relay --afk` session (user request). <!-- children:3b18,6366,bae5,d187 --> <!-- id:d2cd -->

## mechanization (all skills)

- [ ] **[INPUT — meeting] A shared "reasoning-fallacy checkup" step for `/relay` and `/meeting`** (user 2026-07-17: "add TODO for /relay and /meeting: a not-invented-here (and other fallacies?) checkup step"). Both skills already encode anti-fallacy rules as **scattered prose the model may or may not recall** — CLAUDE.md's no-NIH rule, "verify before asserting", "observe before preventing", "constraint archaeology", "prefer dissolving over guarding", the id:415b determinism gate. There is no point at which any of them is *checked*. **EVIDENCE FROM ONE SESSION (2026-07-17), which is why this is not hypothetical — the same session both violated and honoured these rules, with no mechanism deciding which:** (a) **NIH, violated by the apex**: counting own repos, I ran a `~/src/*` glob — exactly what [[use-existing-tools]] bans ("relay.toml is THE own-repo set; never re-derive it from a `~/src/*` glob"). It silently included vendored clones (manim, whisper.cpp, alsa-ucm-conf) and missed the zkm plugins, producing a wrong figure I nearly argued from. `lib-own-repos.sh` existed the whole time. (b) **NIH, honoured by an executor**: id:34c2's child chose to shell out to the real `todo-conformance.sh` rather than copy its regex, so the two definitions of "conforming line" cannot drift. (c) **NIH, honoured by another executor**: id:1102's child factored a *third* copy of the `relay_FILES` awk parser into one shared function. (d) **VERIFY-BEFORE-ASSERTING, violated twice by the apex on ONE item**: id:1102 was filed with root cause "the hand-maintained list drops files" (FALSE — both files were listed) and then "make status is per-skill not per-file" (FALSE — it prints the exact file). Each check took **one command**. Had an executor been dispatched on either, it would have faithfully built the wrong thing. **THE OPEN QUESTION IS WHICH FALLACIES AND WHERE — do not just bolt on a checklist:** candidates are NIH (is there an existing tool? did I grep `scripts/`, the skill's Shared-resources list, the stated source-of-truth?), **assert-before-verify** (the session's most expensive failure — is this claim checked, or inferred?), symptom-vs-root-cause, premature abstraction / gold-plating, and confirmation bias in diagnosis (I kept finding causes that fit my first frame). **Design tensions the meeting must resolve:** (1) **a checklist is prose too** — the very failure mode is "prose the model doesn't recall", so a prose checkup may not beat the prose rules it replaces; what is *mechanizable* here (a `grep` for existing tooling before a new script? a "name the command that proves this" gate on root-cause claims?) versus what is irreducibly judgement — CLAUDE.md mechanize-first says mechanize what can be, and make the residual fail LOUDLY. (2) **per-prompt ctx multiplier** — /relay and /meeting are heavy already; a checkup step multiplies by session count (the CLAUDE.md ctx-budget rule for mandatory steps). (3) **where does it fire** — at handoff (before a spec is written), at review (before a verdict), at meeting decision points, or all three? A check that fires after the spec is written is too late; (d) above shows the damage lands *in the spec*. (4) **the id:de36/id:1102 lesson applies to this item itself**: a checkup nothing invokes is not a checkup. Relates [[use-existing-tools]], [[mechanization-415b]], [[no-labels]], [[mechanize-reliab]], CLAUDE.md §"Use existing tools; ask when unsure" + "Verify before asserting" + §Design heuristics. See `docs/meeting-notes/2026-07-17-1541-semver-trigger-and-fleet-changelog.md` (session context). <!-- id:0e56 -->

- [ ] **[/meeting] REVIEW_ME box freshness vs the ledger — a stale "RUN /meeting" box re-surfaced a settled item** (observed 2026-07-14) — the no-subject `/meeting` audit adds a synthetic Class-3 candidate for open REVIEW_ME boxes and treats a box's "RUN /meeting on id:X" text as a live request. A box can go STALE: id:9fdb's 2026-07-13 "RUN /meeting" box survived a 2026-07-14 TODO re-lane that settled the item (`[INPUT — meeting]`→`[HARD — pool]`, "meeting already held, mtg 1239 D4"), because nothing reconciles a REVIEW_ME box against the referenced id's CURRENT decision/lane state in TODO/ROADMAP → a redundant-meeting recommendation (caught this session only by reading the ratified source). The id:37ab classify fix closes the CLASSIFIER vector but NOT this REVIEW_ME-box vector. **Directions:** (a) when surfacing an open box that references `id:X`, cross-check X against TODO/ROADMAP — if X is now `[x]`, or re-laned off a meeting lane, or carries a DECIDED/RE-LANED note dated after the box, flag it `possibly-stale` and DON'T recommend a meeting off it; (b) mechanize a box↔ledger freshness lint in `orphan-scan.sh`; (c) accept the reviewer-prune cadence as the only guard + document it. Observe-first: FIRST observed instance — prefer the cheap surface-flag (a) over building (b) now. Instance of the "check a derived doc against its ratified source before a pre-registered rule fires" heuristic. **OWNER RULING 2026-07-16 (relay human): PRIORITIZED — the observe-first gate is now DISCHARGED; this is no longer a single instance.** A 5-classifier `/relay human --all` sweep produced **hard recurrence evidence across 4 repos in one pass**: of 6 tier-(a) auto-answers, **3 were stale-box closures rather than verdicts** — cyclotomic-projection `REVIEW_ME:122` asserted "ROADMAP is DRAINED (0 open items)" when `grep -c '^- \[ \]' ROADMAP.md` = **2** (and "11 un-promoted" when the real count was 13); collaib `REVIEW_ME:254` asserted "14 orphan header stubs" when only **3** headers exist and 4 of its 14 listed ids have zero occurrences; cyclotomic `REVIEW_ME:148` asked to confirm a default-flip the owner had already REVERSED and shipped (id:e52d). Two classifiers independently named the pattern unprompted ("reviews are minting boxes faster than they prune them"). **The measurable shape is that a box asserts COUNTS/STATE that are cheaply re-derivable and go wrong silently** — which is what makes direction (b) mechanizable: a lint that re-checks a box's own asserted counts against the live ledger would have caught all 3. Recommend (a)+(b) together now rather than (a) alone; (c) is refuted — the reviewer-prune cadence is exactly what failed here (these boxes survived multiple review passes). Sibling vector: the 2026-07-16 sweep also found a box's file:line SHIFTS under a concurrent review rewrite (yinyang `3709` moved :45→:75 mid-sweep), so any mechanized check must anchor on the id, never a line number. <!-- id:2e5c -->

- [ ] [ROUTINE] @container **[HIGH PRIORITY] Memory-index integrity: nothing verifies that `MEMORY.md` still points at every memory** (user 2026-07-10, prompted by an LLM compaction pass rewriting all 105 index hooks with only *prompt-level*, self-checked invariants — the "documented, not enforced" anti-pattern [[feedback-enforce-not-document-contracts]] names). **The failure is NOT hypothetical and NOT compaction-specific: measured 2026-07-10, the dir holds 108 memory files but the index carries 105 pointers — `feedback-canonical-paths.md`, `feedback-fable-optional-not-gate.md`, `relay-fable-down-two-switch.md` have NO index line and are therefore invisible to recall** (the index is what loads each session; the files are dead weight). Verified pre-existing (absent from the pre-compaction snapshot), so the leak is the **append** path — a memory file written, its `MEMORY.md` pointer never added — not a rewrite. **Cheap because the before-state is free:** `~/.claude/projects` is its own git repo and `MEMORY.md` IS tracked there (hourly `sessions(<host>)` auto-commits), so a check diffs the worktree against `git show HEAD:<path>` — no snapshot plumbing, and today's losses are recoverable from history. **MECHANICAL tier (pure function, ≥2 consumers = append path + any compaction/hand-edit ⇒ passes the id:415b determinism gate):** a `memory-index-lint.sh` asserting (1) dir↔index **bijection** (file with no pointer / pointer with no file — catches the 3 live orphans), (2) vs HEAD: entry count, the set of `(name.md)` link targets, every `id:`/`routed:` token and `[[wiki-link]]` **per entry**, and status lexemes (SHIPPED/DEFERRED/REJECTED/CLOSED/GATED/NO-GO) preserved verbatim, (3) size ceiling. Fail LOUD, non-zero. Wire as a PostToolUse hook on Write/Edit to `MEMORY.md` so it *enforces* rather than advises. **IRREDUCIBLE residual → independent review, narrowly scoped:** a hook can preserve every token yet drift in meaning ("defer refuter fleet" → "refuter fleet" inverts it). Mechanical cannot decide that; an LLM reviewer should fire ONLY on entries whose hook text changed, and must fail loudly ([[feedback-mechanize-reliability-not-cost]] — no LLM where mechanical is ≥ as good). **STRUCTURAL DISSOLUTION (decide first — this may delete the guard):** every one of the 108 files already carries `description:` frontmatter, so `MEMORY.md` could be **GENERATED** by enumerating the directory, making a dropped pointer *unrepresentable* rather than merely detected — exactly [[ledger-derived-index-decision-2840]]'s md=SSOT/index=cache shape, and "prefer dissolving a problem structurally over guarding it". **Open fork:** hooks are hand-tuned and terser than `description:` today, so generation needs either (a) `description:` becomes the hook (one source, lose the terse/verbose split) or (b) a new `hook:` frontmatter field. Pick the fork before building the lint, else the lint guards a file that's about to become derived. **PARTIAL FIX LANDED 2026-07-10** (~/.claude/projects commit 83d81fa0): the 3 orphans are resolved — `relay-fable-down-two-switch` + `feedback-fable-optional-not-gate` now carry index lines (the former SUPERSEDES `fable-down-flag`: it records the user calling `-d` mis-designed after an outage cost 18 handbacks — it was invisible to recall for ~4 weeks), and `feedback-canonical-paths` was an exact duplicate of `feedback-edit-canonical-paths` and was deleted. The size pressure was resolved by **archiving, not truncating**: 10 settled index lines moved to `MEMORY.archive.md` (files untouched, `[[wiki-links]]` still resolve), 20852→17002 bytes with ZERO hook degradation — the same doctrine as `archive-done.sh`. **This CHANGES the lint's contract:** the dir↔index bijection must union `MEMORY.md` ∪ `MEMORY.archive.md`, and the size ceiling applies to `MEMORY.md` alone. Also add an archive-eligibility rule (never archive a `feedback-*` entry — durable user preferences) and a supersession check (an entry whose hook says SUPERSEDES X should sort above X, or X should be archived). The one-shot invariant checker used for this pass (entries / link targets / per-entry `id:`+`routed:`+`[[link]]`+status-lexeme diff vs baseline) is the lint's spec — mechanize it. **FORK DECIDED + DISSOLUTION SHIPPED 2026-07-10** (dotclaude-skills a4cb9b4; ~/.claude/projects 409ea3cc): chose a new optional `hook:` frontmatter field over reusing `description:` — descriptions are as long or longer than the curated hooks, so `description:`-as-hook would GROW the file the ceiling is trying to shrink, and the two fields have different jobs (relevance summary vs index one-liner). Also added `title:` (the real index carries 103 hand-shortened display titles) and `metadata.archived: true` (archive state lives with the file, no split-brain). Resolution is most-specific-first: `title:`→`name:`→stem, `hook:`→`description:`. `tools/memory-index.py` now GENERATES both index files by enumerating the dir: `--check` exits 1 with a diff (the enforcing lint), `--write` regenerates atomically + idempotently. A dropped pointer is now unrepresentable — verified by deleting one and watching `--check` flag it and `--write` restore it. Ordering uses the existing pointers as a cache; git add-date could NOT serve as the key (41 of 107 files share one bulk-backfill timestamp). `feedback-*` + archived = loud exit 2. Ceiling is measured in UTF-8 BYTES not characters (em-dashes cost 3 — an earlier 'under target' claim was a char count and was actually 214 bytes over). 12 hermetic tests; suite 210 green. **LESSON, recorded because it validates the tiering:** the stopped compaction agent passed every mechanical invariant (tokens/links/status/entry-count) yet silently stripped the `user:` prefix from 14 of 15 feedback hooks and flattened emphasis in 62 more — the exact 'all tokens preserved, meaning drifted' residual. - [ ] **New skill: `rebrand-project` — atomically re-brand/rename a project across git remote + local + Claude state** (user 2026-07-01, motivated by the truncocraft→loderite **rebrand** done semi-manually). - [ ] **Mechanization audit across ALL skills — replace LLM-judgment steps with deterministic scripts, even at the cost of more rigid structure** — user directive 2026-06-21: "review as much mechanization as sensible, even at the expense of requiring more rigid structure of e.g. TODO.md". Principle (see memory [[feedback-mechanize-no-swallow-stderr]]): a step done by per-turn LLM judgment is unrepeatable, untested, and silently wrong on edge cases (the trigger: `/relay reconcile --all` improvised an LLM sweep that swallowed git errors and falsely reported "clean" — fixed mechanically as id:4e14). Where a step has a deterministic answer, it belongs in a tested script with a fixed I/O contract, not in a prompt — and it is acceptable to TIGHTEN the structure of the data the skill reads/writes (TODO.md / ROADMAP.md / meeting-notes / personas.md / REVIEW_ME.md grammar) to make that mechanization possible and robust. **Per-skill review (each = candidate sub-item or /meeting):** (1) **todo-update** — formalize TODO.md grammar (section set, one-line-per-task, `<!-- id:XXXX -->` placement) so add/dedup/mark-done/archive are pure script ops, not "grep + judgment"; the done-verification rule (tests-pass OR user-confirm) could become a machine check. (2) **meeting** — orphan-scan / id-minting / append already scripted; review classify.sh, broker sequencing, and persona/discoveries appends for residual LLM steps; can the action-item ↔ ledger mirroring (Step 5b) be a deterministic linter? (3) **git-diary-workflow** — file-attribution in Step 1c ("yours vs not-yours") is currently judgment; could a session-scoped edit-manifest make it mechanical (ties to id:3558 worktree-per-session)? (4) **relay** — discovery, gate-detection (id:3801), reconcile (now `--all`, id:4e14), human-backlog tiering: which classifier shards are *irreducibly* LLM vs mechanizable (overlaps id:cfa9 discover-speedup). (5) **projects** — `proj` is already a deterministic Python scanner (it was RIGHT when my LLM sweep was wrong) — use it as the model; check the dashboard's prioritization heuristic. (6) **hooks/statusline/tools** — mostly mechanical already; audit for hidden LLM assumptions. **Cross-cutting rule to encode:** ban silent error-swallowing (`2>/dev/null` / `|| true` without a stated reason) in skill scripts — a CI/lint check could enforce it. Method: observe-before-preventing where frequency is unknown (design heuristic), but prefer mechanization wherever the answer is deterministic. Likely wants a `/meeting` to decompose per-skill and decide the structure-rigidity tradeoffs before minting build items. **DECOMPOSED 2026-06-21** (`docs/meeting-notes/2026-06-21-2202-mechanization-audit-skills.md`): ratified the **determinism-gate** (T1 pure-function + T2 ≥2-consumers-or-logged-cost) → tag every step **M(echanize)/G(uard)/K(eep)**; grammar tightening allowed only with **loud rejection** (never silent skip); arguable-judgment → Guard not replacement (manual-merge-over-heuristic). **Finding: relay is already the most-mechanized skill** → cross-reference (id:23fe/cfa9/7ace/4e14), don't re-mint. STAYS OPEN as the tracking umbrella for the 6 children below. <!-- id:415b -->

- [ ] [HARD — meeting] **Fake-Haiku mechanical-dispatch proxy — never spin a real model for a deterministic step** (owner 2026-07-19: "spinning up Haiku for a simple Bash call is moronic; tackle the proxy that fakes Haiku, cf. zelegator/chidiai") — the GENERAL mechanization fix behind the relay's per-round agent hops (discovery-runner, the echo-runner token-trim experiment, any Bash-only agent): a LOCAL API-intercept proxy in front of the model endpoint that SHORT-CIRCUITS a request whose only job is a mechanical tool call (echo-runner-shaped: fixed prompt → run ONE Bash command) — the proxy runs the tool locally and returns a synthetic assistant/tool_result with **ZERO real inference/tokens**; the "model" is faked. This is the "non-LLM dispatch" the Workflow sandbox lacks ([[sandbox-2ec4]]), done as a proxy rather than an in-sandbox primitive. **Fail-OPEN**: if the proxy cannot confidently classify a request as purely-mechanical, pass through to the REAL model — never fake a call that needs judgment. Prior art to reuse (spike first): `tools/model-probe.sh` already navigated the subscription/API path ([[probe-tos-path]]); `~/src/zelegator` (semantic router — local-model serving + routing); `~/src/chidiai` (owner cf.). Constraints to settle: ToS (which limb permits an API-intercept — model-probe settled the subscription path), security (proxy handles creds — the relay-svc/os-users tier is relevant), correctness (fail-open + a whitelist of which agent-types are proxy-eligible, e.g. `echo-runner`). ENABLES id:93fe (off-Workflow driver) and shrinks EVERY relay mechanical hop. **REFINED 2026-07-19 (owner): prefer an EXPLICIT custom-model-name trigger (`agent(prompt, {model:"bash"})`) over fake-Haiku DETECTION** — the caller declares mechanical-ness by construction, dissolving the fail-open eligibility heuristic entirely (no guessing which Haiku calls are safe to fake). Backend is the same local resolver; the open feasibility is whether Claude Code's agent `model` field accepts an arbitrary string ("bash") and can route it to a local endpoint PER-AGENT (leaving judgment agents on the real model) — and whether the Workflow sandbox permits that override at all (if not, the trick only helps off-Workflow/host dispatch, id:93fe). Relates id:65f9, id:4d8e, id:2ec4, id:931c (custom agent types), [[sandbox-2ec4]]. **SPIKE 2026-07-19 (conditional GO, OFF-WORKFLOW scope only):** Workflow-internal is NO-GO (id:2ec4 — the sandbox has no net/env/shell; you can't run a proxy inside it, and `agent()` is the only way to shell out). CC subagents share ONE GLOBAL `ANTHROPIC_BASE_URL` (no per-agent endpoint routing — 2026-06-11 note), so you can't point `model:"bash"` at its own endpoint. Instead: a single host-proxy (fronting the off-Workflow driver's traffic) keys eligibility on the request BODY — either `model=="bash"` (EXPLICIT opt-in — dissolves the silent-false-positive risk) OR an exact system-prompt+tools HASH-match of echo-runner (fallback if CC rejects an arbitrary model string — VERIFY via claude-code-guide). Reuse `meeting/contrib/llm-proxy.py` (id:e905, validated transport) — 176f is its deferred request-mutation branch; `~/src/zelegator` `dispatcher.py` = the eligibility→local-vs-passthrough pattern; `~/src/chidiai` has NO proxy code (owner cf. was a mis-pointer, but its cases on zelegator's proxy-design-gone-wrong are a PROCESS warning). **ToS OPEN**: declining-to-send-a-request ≠ vendor-substitution (the reason the llama-proxy was killed) — a materially different posture NOT yet reasoned by any meeting; needs a one-line check pre-build. **Payoff = WALL-TIME** (~18 serialized echo-runner round-trips/run off the critical path), not cost (cache-read is ~0.1× discounted). **Risk #1**: a false-positive fabricates an unreviewed "success" with zero reasoning (worse than an LLM mistake) — mitigate with exact-hash-gate + whitelist=echo-runner-only + version-pin to the agent def. **CRUX RESOLVED 2026-07-19 (claude-code-guide): the `model:"bash"` EXPLICIT trigger IS viable and WINS over hash-matching** — CC accepts an arbitrary `model` string and passes it VERBATIM to the endpoint (no client-side validation once `ANTHROPIC_BASE_URL` is set), so the local proxy SEES `"bash"` in the request body and short-circuits it; the standard Anthropic API would 400, but the proxy intercepts first. Confirmed constraint: `ANTHROPIC_BASE_URL` is GLOBAL-per-process — no per-agent endpoint routing (open FR anthropics/claude-code#38698) — so the single proxy fronts ALL the driver's traffic and routes by the model field (`model=="bash"`→run-locally; else→forward to real Anthropic). The explicit-opt-in trigger therefore DISSOLVES risk #1 (no fabrication of a mechanically-misclassified judgment call — the caller declared it). Hash-match fallback no longer needed. Design SETTLED; remaining before build = the ToS one-liner + reuse e905 transport. Relates id:e905, id:3a1c. **FABLE REVIEW + OWNER CORRECTION 2026-07-19:** Fable flagged (R1) arbitrary-code-exec — the proxy would run whatever Bash is in the request body → **FIX (owner): the proxy runs a RELAY-COMMAND ALLOWLIST only** (exact relay-script invocations); a non-whitelisted command → fail-OPEN passthrough (NEVER executed). Fable's (R5) "whole-session MITM + response-forging + credential SPOF" → **NOT a MITM**: the gateway is PLAIN HTTP (no TLS, no cert forging — per a zelegator check that the base-URL gateway works over http), a legitimate local gateway. Fable's (R3) "consumer evaporated / Workflow-internal NO-GO" is **REFUTED by the owner with prior measurement**: the WORKFLOW ITSELF is the prime consumer — a ~30-min pool measured spending only ~12 min on productive LLM work (the mechanical echo-runner hops ARE the waste), and Workflow `agent()` traffic transits the host harness's GLOBAL `ANTHROPIC_BASE_URL`, so the SAME proxy fronts it. (2) **Process substitution (severe):** the cmd-sub guard blocks only `$(`/backtick; `<(...)`/`>(...)` slips through and `/bin/sh`=bash → executed. (3) **Redirection clobber (moderate):** `>`/`>>`/`2>` not treated as separators → allowlisted script's output written to an attacker path. The same adversarial reviewer that broke it re-attacked the fix: all 3 original bypasses CONFIRMED CLOSED, no new exploitable holes (CR-separator + ANSI-C `$'\x3e'` proven benign — bash refuses/literalizes them too; symlink/env-override/TOCTOU all require already owning the trusted install dir). 18 refusal assertions with real non-execution marker checks (genuinely bite); suite 271/0/0. - [ ] **[exploratory] RED-tests / re-checkable acceptance for META-decisions (design decisions themselves), not just code** (user 2026-07-11, meeting 1239) — design/meeting decisions currently have no analogue to the executor's RED-test bar; a decision can drift or be quietly reinterpreted with nothing to catch it (cf. the "check a derived doc against its ratified source" heuristic, and today's af04 reversal). - [ ] **`relay-events.jsonl` `ts` is NOT an event timestamp — it is a stale round-state snapshot** (observed 2026-07-10 while watching a live pool). `relay-loop.js:58` stamps every event with `state.ts`, the most recent **bash-produced** state timestamp, because the Workflow runtime forbids `Date.now()`/`new Date()` (noted at `relay-loop.js:53`). Consequences: (a) all events emitted within a round share one `ts`; (b) an `integrate` can carry an *earlier* `ts` than a `dispatch` that happened before it; (c) observed in the wild, two `integrate` lines in the same run disagreed on clock — one read `ts=12:43:00Z` beside `ckpt=relay-ckpt-…-1243` (local time, mislabelled `Z`), the other `ts=10:52:06Z` beside `ckpt=…-1251` (true UTC). Net: **event ordering and elapsed-time cannot be derived from `ts`**, and any future `--since` filter, burn-rate attribution, or forensic replay built on it is unsound. Fix options: mint the stamp in the shell producer that actually emits each event (`relay-state-write.sh event-append` already runs bash — stamp there, `date -u`, one clock), or add a monotonic `seq` counter per run and order by that. Audit every ISO stamp under `relay/scripts/` for `date -u` vs local-`date`+`Z` mislabelling while in there. Motivating incident: a monitoring predicate keyed on the event log matched six-day-old events; see the consumer's case notes. <!-- id:d484 -->

- [ ] **An injected unit consumed by `inject.sh take` but never dispatched is INVISIBLE** (observed 2026-07-10). `inject.sh add` mints a token and `take` consumes it in the discovery prelude, but **no event of any `kind` is written for either** (`grep -c '"kind":"inject' relay-events.jsonl` → 0, ever). So the only evidence that an injection was consumed is the token's *disappearance* from `inject.sh peek` — an absence, not a record. If the pool takes a unit and then drops it (verdict mis-mapped, filtered by an exclude/blocked path, lost across a round boundary), there is **no way to distinguish "consumed and dispatched" from "consumed and lost"**, and the user's work silently evaporates. Emit `{"kind":"inject-take","token":…,"repo":…,"verdict":…}` at consume time and carry the token onto the resulting `dispatch`/`integrate`/`handback` events so an injection is traceable end-to-end. Pairs with id:d484 — both are gaps in the relay's own observability, and both were found by a consumer trying to *watch* a pool rather than run one. <!-- id:f3a0 -->

- [ ] [INPUT — meeting] **Broker-backed PARALLEL human-decision channel for the relay-loop (reuse meeting-rpg `broker.py`)** (user 2026-06-30, "just thinking") — today the loop's human-needed cases either HAND BACK + stop or get buried in `RELAY_STATUS.md`, and the Workflow pool **cannot call `AskUserQuestion` at all**, so it can't ask the human anything mid-run. Still its own meeting for transport/auth/consume-side/standalone-mode; folds in [[hermes-deferral-contract]] + [[feedback-ping-threshold-anomalies]] (queue-depth-while-drained = the PING trigger). <!-- id:b444 -->

- [ ] [INPUT — meeting] **Continuous (streaming) dispatch — refill freed slots immediately instead of waiting for the whole wave's last straggler** (user 2026-06-30, "still not happy") — the self-feeding loop is **round-barriered**: `relay-loop.js` dispatches a wave of ≤`POOL_WIDTH` children, **awaits ALL of them** (a `parallel()`-style barrier), integrates, THEN re-discovers and dispatches the next wave. So one slow child idles the other 4 slots until it finishes — the pool drains to near-zero between waves instead of staying saturated. **Want:** as each child completes (and its integration drains), immediately pull the next-highest-priority unit and dispatch it, keeping ~`POOL_WIDTH` units in flight continuously — the Workflow `pipeline()` no-barrier-between-stages model rather than `parallel()` per wave. **Why it's non-trivial (design judgment → meeting):** (1) the **serialized integrator** must stay sequential (one push per repo per turn, D5/D6) — a streaming dispatcher needs a single integrator-consumer draining a completion queue, not N concurrent merges; (2) the **D3 anti-gaming verdict-class order** (execute→review→hard→handoff: unaudited work reviewed before fresh strong work) must still hold when *refilling* — can't stream a handoff for a repo whose review is still pending; (3) **per-repo lease** (id:0902) means never two in-flight units for the same repo — the refill picker must skip repos with a live child; (4) the round-boundary **stop/quota/two-dry-discovery checks** (and the STOP sentinel) must be re-expressed as streaming conditions (ties to id:0ee6 inotify wake + id:c3a6 sig-cache for cheap incremental re-discovery); (5) **fairness/starvation** — a steady stream of high-priority units shouldn't starve a low-priority repo forever. Likely a `[HARD — meeting]` to pick the scheduler shape (continuous picker + bounded in-flight set + single integrator drain), then a `[HARD — pool]` build. Payoff: no more 4-idle-slots-waiting-on-1-straggler; wall-clock tracks the *sum* of work over `POOL_WIDTH`, not the *slowest child per wave* × rounds. **MEETING 2026-06-30-1523 (id:4d8e) decided the SHAPE:** `relay-loop.js` is a Workflow script (sandbox — NO `require`/`import`), so npm job-queue libs (p-queue/bullmq/piscina) are RULED OUT; reuse the harness's own **`pipeline()`** (no-barrier) + the existing per-repo `integrationChains` Map (`:1719`, serialized integrator) — switch the dispatch wave from `parallel()` (`:1685` barrier). Each macro-iteration: cheap mechanical re-discovery (id:4d8e classifier) of all ready units → sort by D3 priority-class rank → feed `pipeline()`. Invariants fall out of existing machinery (serialized integrator = chains; per-repo lease = id:0902; D3 = pre-sort; stop/quota/two-dry = macro-boundary checks); **fairness/starvation is the only genuinely new design.** True mid-flight refill (raw Promise.race picker) = thin follow-on, gated on measurement showing the macro-boundary still idles slots. GATED behind the id:4d8e classifier; build is `[HARD — pool]`. <!-- gated-on:4d8e --> <!-- id:80b8 -->
- [ ] **`inotifywait` (or similar) to make the empty-discovery round unnecessary** (user 2026-06-30) — the self-feeding pool loop ends on (among other conditions) **two consecutive empty discoveries** = it re-shards/re-classifies every own repo a final time just to confirm "nothing new", which is wasted classifier work (and on a `/loop` cadence, repeated every tick over a drained backlog). **Idea:** watch the inputs that a discovery actually reads — the own-repos' ledger files (`ROADMAP.md`/`TODO.md`/`REVIEW_ME.md`), the relevant git refs/`HEAD`, `inject.sh` queue, the shared inbox — with `inotifywait` (Linux; `fswatch` as the portable fallback) so the loop **blocks until something a discovery cares about actually changes**, instead of spinning a confirm-empty round. Turns the drained-pool tail from "poll N repos to find nothing" into "sleep until a real edit/commit/inject arrives". Ties to the **discovery signature cache** (id:c3a6, `discover-sig.sh` already hashes the superset of discovery inputs) — the inotify watch-set should be derived from the SAME input set the sig hashes, so the two can't disagree (a change that flips the sig must wake the watcher, and vice-versa). (NB: unrelated to "inflownistration" — that is a project-domain term, see glossary id:2a3d, not a watcher concept.) Design Qs: which exact paths to watch per repo (reuse the sig's input list), debounce coalescing, how it composes with the existing two-dry-discovery exit (replace it, or gate it), and whether it belongs in `relay-loop.js` (in-session) vs the outage-watchdog/`/loop` layer. Note the [[babysitter-durable-cron-no-op]] constraint: an in-session inotify wait dies with the session — it optimizes a *live* loop's idle tail, it is not an outage-survival mechanism (that's id:98f0). Likely `[HARD — meeting]`. **MEETING 2026-06-30-1523 (id:4d8e) decided + DE-PRIORITIZED:** inotify REPLACES the sleep-poll, NOT the two-dry exit (which stays the correctness condition); watch-set derives from `discover-sig.sh`'s input superset + the b444 decision-queue watchfile (id:de31/b444); fail-safe toward re-checking (overflow/doubt → poll). **GATED behind the classifier (id:4d8e) and de-prioritized — DP1 going mechanical already delivered the headline payoff (dry re-discovery is now near-zero-token bash).** Per user note: `git status` incl. worktree heads is the dominant change signal (already hashed by discover-sig), so it works with or without inotify — inotify is optional polish. Decide if the inotifywait dep is worth it only AFTER the classifier lands. <!-- id:0ee6 -->
- [ ] **Batch-review identical mechanical fan-out commits instead of one strong-turn review per repo** (flagged 2026-06-30 `/relay --afk`) — when one logical change cascades the SAME mechanical diff across N sibling repos, the classifier emits an independent `review` unit per repo and the pool spends one Opus review-child apiece on near-identical diffs. Observed: the Option B ledger migration (`docs(todo): promote to own ledger (Option B, zkm f98d)`) landed one byte-similar commit in 10 zkm-* plugins, each becoming its own `review` verdict (their first audit since the migration was done in-session "no live relay pool"). Same shape recurs on **zkm-version-cascade `uv.lock` bumps** (a parent bump rewrites every plugin's lockfile — see CLAUDE.md versioning). Real spend, low marginal risk: ten reviews of essentially one change. **Idea:** detect a fan-out cohort — commits since last ckpt across multiple repos sharing a near-identical diff / subject / `id:`/`routed:` token — and verify the cohort in ONE pass (review the canonical diff once, confirm each repo's instance matches, checkpoint all), instead of fanning out a review-child per repo. Must stay anti-gaming-safe: still audits every commit (D3), just amortizes the judgment over the cohort rather than re-deriving it N times. Open design Qs: how to recognize "same mechanical diff" robustly (token match? normalized-diff hash? subject prefix?), and where it slots (classifier cohort-grouping vs a review-child that takes a repo-list). Likely `[HARD — meeting]` once scoped. <!-- id:ded2 -->
- [ ] **Review re-derivation must verify conjunctive done-claims per-conjunct, and must NOT accept "tests green" as evidence for an un-encoded clause** (caught 2026-06-30 `/relay review zkm`; case study `chidiai/docs/cases/2026-06-30-done-claim-tests-green-untested-clause.md`). A reverse-handoff executor marked zkm ROADMAP `id:f1d7` ("unify `build_index` TOCTOU guard **+ surface dropped files**") `[x]`/"608 green" while the "surface dropped files" clause was implemented on only **1 of 2** code paths (incremental logged; full-rebuild dropped silently) and **no test encoded it**. The merge subject even hedged "**incremental** … log surface" yet ticked the whole item. The false `[x]` survived one full review cycle + sat as `ROADMAP[x]/TODO[ ]` cross-ledger drift before the next review caught it. **Two process gaps in `references/review.md` step "re-derive roadmap":** (1) a ROADMAP `[x]` whose acceptance text is **conjunctive** (`+` / "and" / "both" / a comma-list of deliverables) must be re-derived **per conjunct** against the diff — verifying the salient/tested conjunct and inferring the rest is the partial-truth trap in completion form; (2) "the suite passes" is **proxy evidence**, never proof of a clause **no test covers** — when a conjunct (esp. a "surface it / don't silently drop / no silent caps" requirement, which adds no happy-path behaviour) has no encoding test, the reviewer must either grep the diff to confirm it landed on **every** relevant path or DEMOTE the item to not-done. **Build surface:** (a) tighten the review reference's re-derivation checklist with the per-conjunct + untested-clause rules; (b) optional `roadmap-lint.sh`/doctor heuristic — flag a freshly-`[x]` item whose acceptance text is conjunctive AND whose touched files added no test, as a review-must-re-derive candidate (folds into id:09a3 grammar-lint / id:0907 doctor); (c) reinforce "separate the *promote* from the *verify*" — a reverse-handoff that promotes AND self-verifies in one pass is its own reviewer (the structural setup for the unverified `[x]`). Relates to the D3 anti-gaming invariant the relay already encodes. <!-- id:369c -->
- [ ] **Uniform scope-arg grammar across `/relay` sub-modes — `--all` | `<repo-list>` | current-only** (user directive 2026-06-23, hit during `/relay human --all`) — `/relay human --all` passed `--all` straight to `gather-human-backlog.sh`, which treated it as a **repo name** and printed `--all path not found (/home/tobias/src/--all) … skipped` then silently scoped to nothing; the no-arg form is what actually means "all own repos". The SKILL.md front-door advertises `--all` for human/review but the underlying collector doesn't parse it. **Directive:** every `/relay` sub-mode (`human`/`review`/`handoff`/`reconcile`/`next`) should accept a consistent scope grammar — **`--all` = all confirmed own repos, an explicit `<repo-list>` = those repos, otherwise imply current-repo-only** (`git rev-parse --show-toplevel`, the review-default-flip convention) — **EXCEPT bare `/relay` (the autonomous loop/pool), which implies `--all` by design.** A bare `--all` token must NEVER be silently consumed as a repo path; an unrecognized scope token is a LOUD reject (id:415b grammar rule), not a silent empty scope. Fix surface: teach `gather-human-backlog.sh` (and the per-mode arg parsing in SKILL.md + the helper scripts) to recognize `--all`/`--current`/repo-list uniformly; add a test that `--all` scopes to all own repos and that bare `<repo>` / no-arg behave per the grammar. Natural fold into the relay-health/grammar work (id:09a3 lint, id:0907 doctor). <!-- id:a02c -->

- [ ] **Doctrine: direct-to-main hotfixes in relay-managed repos must leave an audit record** — gap surfaced 2026-06-29 (zkm, index TOCTOU crash). A main session fixed a live production blocker directly (zkm commit `6dc0132`, filed retroactively as zkm TODO id:f1d7) instead of going through executor→review; the fix was correct but landed *unaudited* and made review-worthy judgement calls (silent-skip vs log; sibling TOCTOU left unfixed) unilaterally. **Rule to encode:** bypassing the executor→review round for an active blocker is fine; bypassing the *record* is not — in the SAME push, file a REVIEW-flagged ledger item recording the commit, why review was skipped, and any unilateral judgement calls, so the next review pass verifies it. **Two-surface fix (per the where-analysis this session):** (1) **canonical doctrine** → add a short `## Direct-to-main hotfixes` section to `relay/references/executor-contract.md` (single source `/relay executor` loads + reviewers cite); (2) **reach the skill-less session** (the actual failure mode is a quick-fix session that NEVER loaded `/relay executor`) → one **self-gating** line in global `~/.claude/CLAUDE.md` Design heuristics: "Relay-managed repos (ROADMAP.md + RELAY_LOG.md present): a direct fix without loading /relay executor is OK for an active blocker, but file a REVIEW-flagged ledger item in the same push." **Rejected:** editing each relay repo's `## Relay contract` CLAUDE.md pointer — ~10 repos + a `v5→v6` stamp bump for one line; global+canonical gets the same reach for two edits, no stamp churn. **Open judgement call** (why this is filed, not self-applied): confirm the self-gating global line is worth the per-prompt ctx cost in EVERY non-relay project (the user's own "per-prompt ctx multipliers" heuristic) vs. accepting that only skill-loading sessions get the rule. - [ ] [INPUT — meeting] ** Inter-session communication / coordination channel — let concurrent sessions notify each other about collisions** — user 2026-06-23, prompted by the observed `meeting-pool-claim-asymmetry-incident` (a loop pool held a trAIdBTC `review` claim + worktree while a parallel `/meeting` + manual `/relay review & handoff` edited the SAME repo's main-checkout ledgers; the collision was only caught because the *human* noticed and manually told the other session). **The gap:** today's coordination primitives are all PASSIVE/one-sided — `claim.sh` leases (id:0902/ebfb) record who holds a repo but only the relay pool acquires/honors them (a `/meeting` or manual main-checkout edit takes no claim, so the lease is asymmetric — see the incident memory); `RELAY_STATUS.md`/`relay-events.jsonl` are write-only logs nobody is *notified* from; the `/meeting`-hold consumer + `.meeting-deferred-writeback.json` (id:2c42) only defer, they don't *talk back*. There is no ACTIVE channel by which session A ("I'm about to review trAIdBTC") learns session B is mid-`/meeting` on it, or by which a human-initiated session announces intent to a running pool. **Discuss (→ /meeting):** (a) what's the right channel — a shared advisory claim that BOTH `/meeting`/manual relay AND the pool acquire+honor (closes the one-sided-lease asymmetry; cheapest, composes with existing claim.sh), a notify/inbox file sessions poll, a `PushNotification`/desktop-notify on contended-claim, or a richer message bus; (b) push vs pull (does the pool poll for "another session wants this repo", or does the claimant signal interrupt?); (c) what's actually worth communicating — repo-level intent, item-level (`id:`), "I'm about to push", "please yield"; (d) granularity vs noise (don't rebuild a chat system for a rare event); (e) human-in-the-loop — is the human the channel (as today, works but manual) acceptable until frequency justifies automation. **Observe-first (user's standing heuristic):** the claim-asymmetry incident is the FIRST logged instance — gate any build on ≥2–3 recurrences; this item is the DISCUSSION placeholder, not a build mandate. Relates [[relay-dispatch-safety-cluster]] (task-claim primitive + /meeting-hold), [[relay-local-parallelism-d2]] (id:c144 exempts /meeting ledger writes from the HARD lease — but exemption ≠ an advisory claim the pool honors; this is the missing half), id:0902 (lease), id:2c42 (deferred write-back), id:c012 (`/relay stop` — one concrete message a channel would carry), id:98f0/e149 (watchdog heartbeat — a related shared-state signal). **UPDATE 2026-06-23 (incident resolved):** the collision resolved with NO data loss — the pool's `execute` child detected the dirty main checkout and HANDED BACK (**id:aa93** dirty-main-checkout guard), refusing to clobber the `/meeting` edits; review still wasted work on a stale base. **Reframes urgency:** data-safety is ALREADY handled by id:aa93, so a coordination channel is about avoiding *wasted stale-base work* + surfacing intent (and saving the human from being the manual relay), NOT preventing corruption — a lower-priority bar. Strengthens observe-first: the backstop held. **SECOND INSTANCE 2026-06-23 (truncocraft — crosses the ≥2-recurrence gate → now build-warranted, not just a placeholder):** parallel `/meeting` saw octahedron.ts/chunkmesh.ts dirty in main; the WIP DIVERGED from the pool execute child's *committed* worktree branch (two different octant-mesher rewrites) and the child's process had DIED while its claim still read LIVE (fresh mtime + worktree-commits = id:7570 heuristic; claim.sh can't see a dead pid). Worse class — id:aa93 does NOT cover it (already committed to its branch) — resolved cleanly only by integrator timing. **Lease-not-exclude lesson (user course-correction):** to reserve truncocraft for a dedicated session, first reached for a `relay.toml` `excluded` edit; user "can't you just use the flock mechanism?" → used a `claim.sh` lease (`relay-reserve-da09-octant`) instead (non-destructive, avoids the id:d530 anti-pattern). Confirms the lease is the right substrate; the build = make `/meeting` + manual relay ACQUIRE+HONOR the same advisory claim + a contended-claim notify, AND solve the ~30-min-TTL durable-reservation gap. See truncocraft TODO id:da09; full detail in the incident memory. — **DECIDED 2026-07-11 (meeting 2026-07-11-1239, amendment A1):** build the bilateral honored-claim — the non-holder DEFERS its ledger write via the id:2c42 drop-file (replay on release); forbid raw-`Edit` ledger writes (flock'd `md-merge` only); symmetric meeting↔pool. **INTERIM GUARD (partial-supersession, corrected 2026-07-11):** id:5a39 (meeting-as-relay-producer) dissolves only the **`/meeting`-vs-pool ledger-write slice** of this item — it does NOT cover the broader coordination scope (manual `/relay review`-vs-pool collision, contended-claim notify, the ~30-min durable-reservation gap), which survives 5a39. So evaluate 5a39 before building the *meeting-ledger-write* enforcement, but 9000 is NOT fully gated on / superseded by 5a39 — its manual-relay + notify halves stand on their own (dissolve-before-guard applies only to the overlapping slice). <!-- id:9000 -->
- [ ] [INPUT — meeting] ** Item-level claim marker at pick-time (pre-worktree-branching) so concurrent sessions/agents don't double-pick the same TODO/ROADMAP `id:`** — user 2026-07-07, prompted by this session dispatching 4 background executors each on a specific `id:` (6f61/b67e/3558/c79e + b3ee): double-pick was avoided ONLY because the foreground held a *repo-level* meeting claim (`claim.sh acquire dotclaude-skills --mode meeting`), which is coarse — it blocks the whole repo for the duration. - [ ] **Cross-repo routed action items never land in the target repo's tracking — `/meeting`'s "→ routed to <repo> inbox" is a dead letter** — observed 2026-06-18: toesnail's `/meeting` `docs/meeting-notes/2026-06-18-0729-veq-macro-verify-carrier.md` action item `routed:8587` ("→ routed to `mathematical-writing` inbox: design the `.mw` side of the carrier", fulfilling the earlier `routed:e4df` park) was written ONLY in the toesnail meeting note. **`.mw` had no `8587`/`e4df`/`veq`/`carrier` reference ANYWHERE** (TODO/ROADMAP/REVIEW_ME), and `.mw` has no `inbox` file at all — so the routed item was a dead letter for the gap between the meeting (2026-06-18) and a human noticing it. The `/meeting` skill writes the `routed:<id>` token into the SOURCE repo's note but has no mechanism to (a) create the item in the TARGET repo's ROADMAP/TODO, nor (b) surface "you have N inbound routed items pending ingestion" when the target repo is next worked. Same risk for every `routed:<id>` / `ref:<id>` cross-repo handoff (cf. `dotclaude-skills/TODO.md` already uses `ref:aae4` as a manual guard — that pattern is the workaround, not a fix). **Fix directions:** (1) `/meeting` (and `/relay`), when emitting a `routed:<id>` to another repo, should ALSO append a stub `- [ ] [INBOUND — routed:<id> from <repo>/<note>] <title>` into the target repo's TODO.md (flock'd `md-merge.py`), so the item exists in the target's tracking immediately; OR (2) a cross-repo "inbound routed" scanner (a `scripts/scan-routed.sh` greppable over all `own` repos' meeting-notes for `routed:<id>` whose target repo lacks a matching `id:`/`routed:` line) wired into `/relay` discovery / `/projects` dashboard so dead letters surface. (3) At minimum document the manual ingestion step in `/meeting`'s SKILL.md so the router doesn't assume "routed" = "tracked". This near-miss cost a full design item (`.mw` id:358f) sitting untracked; only caught because the owner manually asked "what about .mw's ROADMAP?". Relates to id:0a1e (auto-surface prior decisions on a known id) — both are "the ledger doesn't know about a decision recorded elsewhere". **LIVE EVIDENCE 2026-06-25 (this item is no longer hypothetical):** while shipping id:2dea (the repo-LOCAL un-promoted-backlog scan), a sweep of the shared inbox found a large stranded backlog — for **this repo alone, 12 open inbound `routed:` items target it yet NONE appear in its TODO/ROADMAP** (dead letters), and ~12 inbox lines are bare prose carrying **no `routed:` token at all**, so `append.sh inbox-done` can never resolve them and no scanner can correlate them (the same id-less blind spot id:2dea's `untracked` disposition closes repo-locally). id:2dea is the repo-LOCAL sibling (open TODO with no ROADMAP twin); **this (id:3947) is the cross-repo / inbox layer** — deliberately out of relay's repo-confirmed scope today (the inbox is "surface-only at `/meeting` step 7b + `/projects`", id:b30b), so do NOT just bolt the inbox onto `unpromoted-scan.sh` (it would couple this PUBLIC repo to the local-only `~/.claude/todo-inbox.md` and cross that boundary). Fix belongs at the `/meeting`+`/projects` layer per the proposals above; the `scan-routed.sh` (proposal 2) **must also flag inbox entries lacking a `routed:` token** (the rot found here), not only target-repo-missing twins. Cousin id:69f4 (cross-project mirrored-id sync). <!-- id:3947 -->
- [ ] **`loop-hint.sh` swallows the `--afk` nudge after a recent prior run (time-gap heuristic too aggressive)** — observed 2026-06-18: a manual `/relay . .mw --afk all \veq and related` printed NOTHING from `loop-hint.sh` (step 0a), so the "wrap this in `/loop` for unattended resilience" tip — the single most useful hint for someone who *just typed `--afk`* (= "I'm walking away") — was suppressed. Root cause: `loop-hint.sh` decides standalone-vs-loop-tick PURELY by time since the last run (`$STAMP` ≤ `GAP`=2700s → assume loop tick → silent). A manual re-invocation within 45 min of any prior `/relay` (very common during an interactive session) trips the suppression even though `--afk` is an EXPLICIT away-signal that should make the nudge fire. The script never even sees argv — the front door calls it with no args. **Fix direction:** pass the invocation's flags into `loop-hint.sh` (or set an env marker) so an explicit `--afk`/`--allow-intensive` **forces** the tip regardless of the time gap. **Nuance (the hard part, already noted in the script header):** a `/loop 20m /relay --afk` would then re-nag every tick, because a manual `--afk` and a loop-driven `--afk` are otherwise indistinguishable (the built-in `/loop` sets nothing observable). So the real fix needs a reliable in-`/loop` marker (env var the loop runner sets, or a sentinel the front door can detect) to separate "manual --afk" (print) from "loop tick of --afk" (suppress). Until that exists, weigh: (a) force-print on `--afk` and accept re-nag on afk-loops (the script already self-suppresses on plain `/relay` loop ticks, so only afk-loops re-nag), vs (b) shorten/condition `GAP` only when `--afk` is present. Low-severity (cosmetic — the nudge is advisory) but it defeats the entire purpose of the 2026-06-18 "surface it FIRST" directive. See `relay/scripts/loop-hint.sh` + SKILL.md step 0a. <!-- id:888a -->

Gates that resolve *outside* the repo change nothing in-repo, so they keep re-emitting as "needs a /meeting" until a human notices: chidiai id:1e77 (≥50 outcome rows accumulate), proton-moresync id:5cc5 (first external user), zomni id:7cf2 (an OOM-kill / PSI-full stall fires), ai-codebench id:efc2 (the 244b GPU matrix run finishes). **Fix directions**: a per-item machine-checkable gate predicate the collector/discovery evaluates (flips gated_hard→actionable when met), or a periodic gate-recheck pass. - [ ] **`/loop /relay` re-fires blindly — no feedback from relay's exit reason (quota cap / pool drain) to suppress or postpone the next cron tick** — observed 2026-06-18: a `/loop 30m /relay --afk …` cron re-fires `/relay` every 30 min on pure wall-clock, regardless of WHY the prior run ended. Two wasteful cases: (1) **quota stop** — relay already knows the guilty bucket's `resetTime` (`quota-stop.sh` returns per-bucket `resetTime`/`pctRemaining`, surfaced in `RELAY_STATUS.md`), but nothing feeds it back, so ticks keep firing into a capped quota until the window happens to reset; the tick should be **postponed until the guilty bucket's reset** (or be a cheap no-op that re-checks quota and exits fast). (2) **pool drain** (two empty discoveries = backlog drained) — re-discovering every 30 min until new work appears is mostly wasted; the loop should back off (longer cadence) or self-terminate until new commits/items land. The hard part is the channel: the built-in `/loop`/cron fires a fixed prompt and has no hook to read relay's exit state — so this needs either (a) the front door writing a machine-readable "next-useful-at" / "stop-reason" stamp (e.g. into `RELAY_STATUS.md` or a sidecar) that an early step of the next `/relay` run reads to decide "exit immediately, nothing to do until T", or (b) a relay-aware loop wrapper that schedules its own next wake from the stop reason (cf. ScheduleWakeup dynamic mode) instead of a dumb fixed cron. Shares the "no reliable in-`/loop` marker" root cause with id:888a (loop-hint can't tell a manual `--afk` from a loop tick — same missing channel). Needs a small design note before building; low-cost-but-non-obvious. <!-- id:8602 -->
- [ ] **Relay executor "Prompt is too long" — the executor prompt embeds the full ROADMAP, so a repo with a large ROADMAP can't be dispatched ANY execute/INTENSIVE work** — observed 2026-06-22 (run relay-20260622-070530-18085): `[execute:ai-codebench] failed: Prompt is too long`. ai-codebench's ROADMAP.md is ~400+ lines (~30 `[x]` done items, each with large Session-note/Done-check/Context prose), and the generated executor contract treats ROADMAP items as "the single source of truth" → the child's prompt overflowed the context limit and the execute unit failed outright. **This is what actually BLOCKED the user's desired overnight `[INTENSIVE]` benchmark** (ai-codebench id:244b/8bea): no execute/intensive dispatch can succeed on that repo until fixed (id:8bea now gated on this). **Fix directions:** (a) pass only the OPEN items (+ the target item's spec) to the child, NOT the full done-item history — done prose has zero value to an executor (the durable fix); (b) ARCHIVE done `[x]` ROADMAP items into a `ROADMAP.archive.md` — the relay has NO ROADMAP archiver today (`todo-update/archive-done.sh` only does TODO.md); generalize it or add a relay equivalent, shrinking the live ROADMAP; (c) detect prompt-size overflow BEFORE dispatch and hand back with a clear "ROADMAP too large — archive/trim done items" reason instead of a generic "Prompt is too long" failure (graceful degradation, cf. id:2d20). Relates to `relay/references/executor-contract.md`, the ROADMAP-as-source-of-truth convention, `todo-update/archive-done.sh`, and id:244b/8bea (the ai-codebench intensive work this gates). **UPDATE 2026-06-22 (investigated — filed premise was WRONG):** the dispatch/executor-contract do NOT inline the ROADMAP — `relay-loop.js unitPrompt` (L888-908) and `executor-contract.md` only POINT to ROADMAP.md; the execute child READS it from its worktree. So the real bloat is (1) the DISCOVERY path — `gather-repo-state.sh` `cat`-ted the FULL ROADMAP into every shard's gather JSON (L107, cf. the id:11ad shard cache_read blowup) → **FIXED**: it now emits OPEN items + structure only with a non-silent omission note (`test_gather_repo_state.sh` case 7; `discover-sig.sh` still hashes the full ROADMAP = a safe superset, so no under-invalidation); and (2) the execute child reading the full on-disk ROADMAP.md → **MITIGATED** by the archiver id:6b67 (keeps the file small). So fix-(a) ≡ the gather-trim is DONE, fix-(b) ≡ the archiver is DONE; only fix-(c) remains — graceful "ROADMAP too large" overflow-detection→handback instead of the bare "Prompt is too long" — now LOW priority since the file/discovery views stay small. **Reduced scope: (c) only.** <!-- id:93cc -->
  - **Child id:6b67 [ROUTINE] — Relay ROADMAP archiver** (`relay/scripts/roadmap-archive.sh`): fix-direction (b) above, spec'd as an executor item in ROADMAP.md (single-id-two-views). Moves done `[x]` ROADMAP item-blocks → `ROADMAP.archive.md` under the same conservative prior-commit/≥30d gate as `archive-done.sh`, no header pruning, flock'd, with `tests/test_roadmap_archive.sh`. - [ ] **Quota decay only covers the 7-day bucket — no 5h-window (or generalized late-window) use-it-or-lose-it decay** — `RELAY_QUOTA_DECAY_7D` interpolates the `seven_day`/`seven_day_sonnet` thresholds START→END against `seven_day.resets_at`, but the **5h bucket has no decay at all** (grep-confirmed 2026-06-18: zero `DECAY_5H`/`FIVE_HOUR` decay in `quota-stop.sh`). User intent (2026-06-18): permitted useup should be **higher late in a window than early** — the last hour of a 5h window / end of a day should allow spending more, since unused quota is lost at reset (back-loaded "0.10:0.70"-style). The existing knob is directional (back-loading already expressible), so the gap is: (1) add `RELAY_QUOTA_DECAY_5H` (interpolate the `five_hour` threshold against `five_hour.resets_at`, mirroring the 7d path in `quota-stop.sh` + forward it through `relay-loop.js` envPairs + document in the knob table); (2) optionally generalize to a single per-bucket decay mechanism so any bucket can carry a `START:END`. Note the direction nuance: the current `RELAY_QUOTA_DECAY_7D` docs/example front-loads (`0.70:0.10`, tighten late) — the user wants the OPPOSITE for use-it-or-lose-it, so document both directions clearly and pick a sensible default for the afk-loop case. Independent of id:8602 but compounding: a late-window-permissive 5h cap + a quota-aware loop tick is the full "spend the window down then sleep till reset" behavior. <!-- id:1ae7 -->
- [ ] **discover-sig.sh: `upstream` field read without a fetch → origin-behind under-invalidation** — audit id:401c Run 11 (`docs/meeting-notes/2026-06-17-1102-strong-model-audit.md`, finding 3.1a). The sig hashes `HEAD...@{upstream}` WITHOUT fetching, but the shard's SYNC-WITH-ORIGIN guard (id:c3f7) fetches+FF. If origin advances between rounds with the local tracking ref untouched, the sig is byte-identical → cached verdict reused, no fetch/FF until the next sig-moving event. Bounded (single pool run, self-healing) but a genuine under-invalidation — the one hazard class the CLAUDE.md gotcha warns about ("new signal → add to discover-sig.sh's blob"). LOW severity. **Needs a measured decision, not an inline edit** (a fetch-per-sig adds network cost to every discovery round) — weigh fetch-in-sig vs accept-the-bounded-staleness. <!-- id:4348 -->
- [ ] **Profile relative intensity of `[INTENSIVE]` tasks → resource-budget co-scheduling instead of blanket serial-alone** — the `[INTENSIVE — <resource>]` mechanism (id:8d52) treats EVERY intensive unit identically: it runs serially-alone after each round's parallel wave, holding an exclusive `resource:<name>` claim. That binary policy was built around the worst case — the OOM-risk local-LLM benchmarks from ai-codebench ([[oom-local-model-session-kills]]: 6 sessions killed when a 26B model ran). But intensive tasks are NOT uniformly heavy: observed 2026-06-22, a `leAIrn2learn` jax/optax ES task uses **one core and leaves plenty of RAM free**, while ai-codebench local-LLM runs are genuinely memory-heavy. Forcing the light one to run alone wastes the idle cores/RAM — the pool sat on a single task while 18 repos were blocked and resources were free. **Direction:** (1) profile/measure per-task footprint (peak RSS, core count, GPU?) — start with a logger that records actual resource use of each intensive run (observe-before-preventing, cf. design heuristics), keyed by repo/item so the data accrues; (2) replace the binary `resource:<name>` exclusive claim with a **resource BUDGET** (e.g. RAM headroom + core count) so light intensive tasks can co-run with each other and/or the normal parallel wave up to the budget, while a heavy one (GPU / large-model / measured high-RSS) still claims exclusivity. Lets `--afk` actually saturate the box instead of idling on one light task. Tag the relative intensity in the `[INTENSIVE — <resource>]` marker or relay.toml (`intensive = "<resource>"` could gain a weight) so the scheduler reads it rather than guesses. Relates id:8d52 (the serial-alone mechanism this refines), id:da26 (`hard` verdict), [[oom-local-model-session-kills]] (the worst case that must keep exclusivity), and the `--allow-intensive`/`--afk` path. Trigger: 2026-06-22 `/relay --afk` session (user observation: "if enough resources are available the loop shouldn't work only on a single task"). <!-- id:c7b6 -->

- [ ] **Self-model guard: default to executor-only after timeout in unattended mode** — **SUPERSEDED 2026-06-15 by the Opus-apex pivot (id:da26, f64c28b):** the self-guard (warn+sleep) is removed; the front door now probes Fable once/2h and defaults to Opus apex (Fable a bonus, never a gate). Resolves the item's intent (never dispatch a doomed strong unit; the long-requested auto-probe shipped at spec level) — kept open only until the probe is a tested helper rather than a front-door instruction. Original: user directive 2026-06-13: when on Opus without `-d` AND the strong tier (Fable) is unavailable, the SKILL.md step-0 guard currently does "warn + `sleep 10` + proceed" — but that "proceed" dispatches strong-model review/handoff units on `claude-fable-5`, which fail when Fable is down (observed thrice 2026-06-13; the 3rd was an **attended `handoff` run** — all 5 fable children returned "Fable 5 unavailable" at launch, operator asked the user → Opus pilot of 2/5). The attended case worked correctly (asked), but reinforces two design facts: (i) **handoff has NO executor fallback** — creating the roadmap IS the strong work — so unattended fable-down must DEFER handoff units entirely (the `-d` semantics already say this; verify the autonomous front door honors it), not merely demote review→execute; (ii) auto-probe would have avoided spawning 5 doomed children. The guard should, **after the timeout with no human abort (i.e. unattended), DEFAULT TO EXECUTOR-ONLY** (`fableDown=true`) rather than launching doomed strong-model units OR auto-escalating to expensive Opus reviews (which must stay explicit `--strong-tier opus` opt-in). Design qs to resolve: (a) how does the front door detect "unattended" vs an interactive operator who'd Ctrl-C? (b) does this fold into the deferred Fable auto-probe ([[fable-down-flag]] notes auto-probe deferred — demand now confirmed thrice)? (c) interaction with `--interactive` flag. Conservative default everywhere: never auto-spend Opus, never dispatch a strong unit you expect to fail. <!-- id:f649 -->
- [ ] **Relay discovery: record canonical repo path at confirm-time (deterministic, not default-path-assumed)** — relay.toml assumes each repo lives at `~/src/<name>`, but the 12 zkm-* plugin repos actually live at `~/src/zkm/plugins/zkm-<name>`. With no `# path:` override the discovery LLM agent was NON-DETERMINISTIC: the 2026-06-13 09:38 `-d` run reported them "missing at ~/src/zkm-*" and deferred them; the 09:54 run's agent improvised, found them under `plugins/`, and executed 7 of them. Same prompt, same config, different agent initiative. **Immediate fix applied 2026-06-13:** added explicit `# path: ~/src/zkm/plugins/zkm-<name>` overrides to all 12 plugin blocks in relay.toml. **Durable fix (this item):** when the orchestrator first confirms a repo (handoff/discover), resolve and persist its canonical path via `git -C <candidate> rev-parse --show-toplevel` into the relay.toml block, rather than relying on the `~/src/<name>` default + manual override. Removes the improvisation surface entirely. Also: discover-repos.sh should emit canonical paths, and the discover agent should treat a default-path miss as a hard "surface for path confirmation", never silently improvise OR silently defer. **UPDATE 2026-06-29 (user, during a `/relay handoff&review --all`):** the gap bit again at the *consumer* layer — a strong-turn ad-hoc cheap-scan improvised a `~/src/<name>` sweep and (a) missed the nested `zkm/plugins/zkm-*` repos and (b) hardcoded the `~/src/` layout. Lesson: **the own-repo set + paths must always be derived from `relay.toml` (honoring `# path:`), never from a `~/src/*` glob** — exactly how `gather-human-backlog.sh` / `relay-reconcile.sh --all` already resolve them. Two asks fold in here: (1) any relay-adjacent scan (incl. front-door cheap pre-scans) should resolve repos via a single shared relay.toml path-resolver, not a directory glob; (2) reconsider whether `# path:` should be a **proper TOML field** (`path = "…"`) rather than a comment-override — a comment is invisible to a naive TOML parse and is the thing that made the override "feel" optional. The durable canonical-path persistence above subsumes (2) if it writes a real field. <!-- id:f5d8 -->
- [ ] **Relay write-status agent leaks a literal `${HOME}/` dir into cwd** — the `writeRelayStatus` agent in `relay-loop.js` is told to write to `~/.config/fables-turn/RELAY_STATUS.md` "expand ~ to $HOME", but on the 2026-06-13 `-d` run it created a literal `${HOME}/.config/fables-turn/RELAY_STATUS.md` under the dotclaude-skills repo root (single-quoted `${HOME}` never expanded), polluting the working tree (showed as untracked `${HOME}/`). Same risk for any agent given a `~`/`${HOME}` path while cwd is a repo. Fix: have the write agent resolve `$HOME` itself (or pass an already-expanded absolute path from the script) and assert the target is absolute before writing. - [ ] **Relay integrator leaves orphan worktrees when a child leaves untracked files** — the serialized integrator's step 5 ran `git worktree remove` (no `--force`), which fails on ANY untracked file in the worktree (e.g. a `uv.lock` a review/execute child generated by running `uv`/tests). Because it's `&&`-chained with `branch -d` and runs after a successful merge+tag+push, the failure silently orphans the worktree AND branch under `~/.cache/fables-turn/worktrees/` (found a helferli review orphan 2026-06-13). **FIX SHIPPED 2026-06-13:** step 5 now uses `worktree remove --force` (safe — the committed branch work is already integrated by that point; --force only discards incidental untracked build artifacts). Verify next multi-review run leaves no orphans, then tick. <!-- id:d187 -->
- [ ] **relay-burn.sh: harden the `report` `date -d "$reset"` awk-shellout against a crafted `resets_at`** — strong-model audit Run 9 (2026-06-16, `docs/meeting-notes/2026-06-16-0928-strong-model-audit.md`, Pass 2) found that `relay-burn.sh report`'s human-table path interpolates the JSONL `reset` field (sourced from `seven_day.resets_at`/`five_hour.resets_at` in `/tmp/claude-usage-cache.json`) directly into a shell command run via awk `getline` (`cmd = "date -d \"" reset "\" +%s …"`). A crafted `resets_at` would be a command-injection seam. **Risk accepted LOW** for now: `resets_at` is provider-controlled API data written by the statusline from `/api/oauth/usage`, and an attacker who can write the cache already has local code execution; the seam is also unexercised by any non-`--json` caller in the relay path. **Fix when convenient:** validate `resets_at` (e.g. `^[0-9T:+\-]+$` guard, or parse the epoch in jq inside `report`'s main jq pass) before any `date -d` shellout. Forward-robustness only. <!-- id:287b -->
- [ ] **Intra-repo parallelism — dispatch >1 unit in the same repo when writes are disjoint** — user 2026-06-15: today the pool parallelizes only ACROSS repos (`POOL_WIDTH` = distinct repos, one unit/repo; the lease `claim.sh` is whole-repo, and the integrator does one `--no-ff` merge + one push per repo per turn). The guardrail already *permits* "within a repo on disjoint paths" but nothing implements it. Motivating use case: **`/relay` scoped to the relay (meta) repo alone, at maximum parallelism** — when dotclaude-skills is the only confirmed repo there's currently nothing to fan out across, so the meta-work serializes. **User's write-disjointness model to validate:** the three relay actors touch shared ledgers in mostly-non-conflicting ways — `REVIEW_ME.md` is *append* by executors, *existing-box edits* by `/relay human`, *read + light tidy* by review; ROADMAP similarly (executors tick `[ROUTINE]` boxes, review re-derives, human/handoff define). So "clearly parallelizable" units (touching disjoint files, or disjoint code paths within one repo) should be safe to run concurrently in the same repo NOW. **Nuance/caveats to design around:** (i) these ledgers are NOT `merge=union` (checkbox `[ ]`↔`[x]` toggles can't union) — concurrent edits still need line-scoped flock'd writes (`meeting/md-merge.py`) and git surfaces residual conflicts (`orphan-scan.sh --cross-ledger`); RELAY_LOG.md *is* union (append-only), so it's the easy case. (ii) integration ordering — N worktrees in one repo all merging to the same branch needs a single-owner serialized merge (the D5/D6 "never two children pushing to the same remote" rule), so the parallelism is in the *work*, not the *push*. (iii) claim granularity must drop from whole-repo to sub-repo (path-set or unit-id) so two same-repo units don't refuse each other's lease. **Phasing:** start with the trivially-disjoint case (units whose file/path sets provably don't intersect — e.g. a doc edit + a test-only change + a script in different dirs), gated by a static path-overlap check; defer less-trivial in-repo parallelism (same-file disjoint hunks, semantic coupling) to a follow-up. **Likely wants a `/meeting`** — non-obvious tradeoffs (worktree-per-unit-within-repo vs single worktree + serialized stages, claim re-granularity, merge ordering, how the discovery classifier emits multiple units per repo and proves their disjointness). Relates to [[parallel-session-state-coordination]] (worktrees scoped to same-repo code edits), id:3558 (worktree-per-session flock'd merge), id:6a3c Axis B (write-contention coupling), and the dispatch-safety cluster. **User comment for the meeting (2026-06-15):** "Why does REVIEW_ME need flock when we're supposedly using worktrees?" — valid challenge: among worktree children flock IS redundant (each child has an isolated working copy; the single-owner serialized merge + git conflict-surfacing handle ordering). The flock'd `md-merge.py` exists for MAIN-CHECKOUT writers that do NOT use a worktree — `/relay human` and `/meeting`/manual edits write REVIEW_ME/ROADMAP/TODO directly in the main checkout, and a live `/meeting` racing a `/relay human` (or the integrator touching main) is a same-directory concurrency hazard. So the rule is: worktree work → serialized merge, NO flock; same-directory work → flock. The earlier framing of this item conflated the two. If intra-repo parallel units ALL ran in their own worktrees, flock is moot for them — which argues for "worktree-per-unit + serialized merge" as the clean design and reserves flock strictly for the non-worktree main-checkout actors. Also: the whole-repo lease is the obvious thing to re-granularize (sub-repo path-set / unit-id leases). <!-- id:ca87 -->
- [ ] [HARD] **Periodic test-integrity sanity-check on a cadence (not just on unaudited commits)** — user 2026-06-16: occasionally a repo should get a dedicated [HARD] sanity check verifying its commits carry red→green justification (test added red → impl change → green), independent of whether there are *new* unaudited commits to review. **Distinct from existing machinery:** `gaming-scan.sh` (mechanical: deleted tests / added skips / removed asserts) and `review.md §2` (resurrection check) only fire inside a `review` unit, i.e. when there ARE unaudited commits since the last ckpt — so a repo that's been quiet (or whose gaming slipped through earlier) is never re-swept. **Likely wants a `/meeting`** (user flagged it).
