- [ ] [ROUTINE] **Pool busy-loops re-dispatching un-doable HARD units → never drains, burns an Opus child + an inject-take per round** — observed 2026-06-16 (run relay-20260616-063457-22124): after the backlog drained, ~15 repos' only open work is [HARD] items that are decision-gated (need a /meeting: isochrone id:b104, zkm-claude-ai id:107, zkm-photo, meeting-rpg) or too-large/cross-repo (zkm-scan id:02bd, zkm-eml id:ff0f). The `hard` classifier emits a unit for each, an Opus child sizes it and correctly HANDS BACK (C5 "don't half-do it"). **Bug:** `runRound()` returns `actionable: actionable.length` (relay-loop.js:1135) = units *dispatched*, not units that *did work*; a handed-back hard unit still counts as actionable, so `dry` resets to 0 every round (line 1159) and the drain-detector (`dry >= 2`) never fires. The loop re-discovers the SAME gated-hard set every round and spins to the `MAX_ROUNDS=30` seatbelt (or quota), re-spawning an Opus child per gated repo per round to re-derive the identical handback, and running one `inject.sh take` per round in the discovery prelude (id:9ed4) on an empty queue — the "mostly nothing + many inject-take dispatches" symptom. Real work still ships (7 checkpoints that run), but most rounds are pure churn. **Fix options:** (a) count only units that produced a checkpoint (or did NOT hand back) toward `actionable`, so an all-handback round is a dry round; (b) per-run memo: once a repo's top HARD item hands back as gated/too-large, suppress it from re-dispatch for the rest of the run (mark the repo "hard-exhausted this run"); (c) durably mark a decision-gated HARD item (e.g. relay.toml `hard_blocked_until` or a ROADMAP tag) so the classifier skips it until a /meeting clears it — surface in RELAY_STATUS Queued instead. (a)+(b) make the loop drain after ONE pass over the gated-hard set instead of 30; (c) stops re-deriving the gate every run. Likely (a) for the immediate bleed + (c) for the durable fix. **PARTIAL FIX SHIPPED 2026-06-16 (branch relay-observability):** (a) `runRound` now returns `produced` (checkpoints integrated this round) and the outer loop's drain counter keys on `produced===0`, so an all-handback round counts as no-progress → drains after 2 rounds instead of spinning to MAX_ROUNDS=30 (test_relay_loop_structure id:2d20 checks); AND the discovery classifier now applies an EXECUTABLE-HARD test — `[HARD — decision gate]` / under-a-Gated-section / acceptance-needs-/meeting / multi-session items are EXCLUDED from the `hard` verdict + openHard and SURFACED ("HARD backlog is gated — needs /meeting") instead of dispatched, so already-gated repos stop spawning an Opus child per round. **STILL OPEN (durable auto-closure, → meeting id:719e):** option (c) — when a strong child hands back a FRESHLY-discovered `[HARD — strong model]` item as too-large/gated, AUTO-re-tag it to `[HARD — decision gate]` (durable, in the ROADMAP via the integrator's main-checkout write path) so it never gets re-dispatched in a LATER run either. Forks: where the durable mark lives (ROADMAP re-tag vs relay.toml field vs sidecar), how it's invalidated when the item is re-scoped, REPORT-schema field for the child to signal it, and trusting the child's one-shot "too-large" verdict. Until (c) lands, a human (or the /meeting) re-tagging the item to `[HARD — decision gate]` durably stops re-dispatch today via the new classifier exclusion. <!-- id:2d20 -->

- [ ] **Orphaned dead-run worktrees with UNMERGED commits accumulate — id:3ac8 surfaces but never resolves them** — user 2026-06-16: "you mentioned dangling worktrees, but /relay didn't pick them up?" Correct — by design the id:3ac8 auto-reap only removes CLEAN worktrees (HEAD is an ancestor of the repo's main → nothing to lose); worktrees carrying unmerged commits are deliberately NOT reaped (never delete unmerged work) and are only SURFACED as "stale worktree from a dead run with N unmerged commit(s) — needs manual integration." But nothing ever integrates them: the serialized integrator only merges worktrees from children IT dispatched this run, not orphans from dead/killed runs, so they pile up and get re-surfaced as HANDBACKs every run. Snapshot 2026-06-16 after stopping run 22124: 10 orphaned worktrees with 1 unmerged commit each — claude-organizer, collaib, linguistic-unversals, mathematical-writing, puzzle-pwa, rawrora (0615), toesnail ×2 (incl. an `ed7fc8ad-handoff`), zkm-ner, zkm-pdf — spanning dead runs from 0615 + this run. **Why they exist:** a child committed in its worktree, then the run died/was-killed BEFORE the integrator merged+pushed (or integration aborted), stranding the commit. **Wanted: an orphan-reconcile path** the pool (or a `/relay reconcile` mode) runs at discovery: for each orphaned worktree with unmerged commits, attempt the standard verify→`--no-ff` merge→ckpt-tag→push→prune IF it applies cleanly to the current main and passes the repo's suite; on conflict/red, leave it and surface ONE actionable line (not silently re-surface every run). - [ ] **Injected unit + same-repo discovery unit in one round → concurrent same-repo units race the integrator → spurious dirty-tree handbacks (wasted strong children)** — observed live 2026-06-16 (run relay-20260616-112222-29307, round 5): an `inject.sh add dotclaude-skills --verdict hard` (id:f6c9) was dispatched in the SAME round dotclaude-skills also had a normally-discovered `review` unit (and an `execute` re-enqueue). All three ran concurrently in separate worktrees; the `hard` child won the integrator, merged + checkpointed (eaf95c6/2571e3f), but its mid-merge writes to the shared MAIN checkout (`~/src/dotclaude-skills`) made the OTHER two units' integration see a dirty tree → both handed back ("Working tree is dirty: relay/references/human.md … Cannot merge"). No corruption (the dirty-tree guard worked), no work lost (they re-dispatch next round) — but two strong/sonnet children were spent for nothing + confusing handback noise. **Root cause (relay-loop.js):** the stated invariant is "pool of distinct repos, one unit per repo" (L71), enforced via the per-repo lease `claim.sh acquire` (L808). BUT (a) the lease is keyed cross-SESSION by runId and `claim.sh acquire` is RE-ENTRANT for the same runId, so two units of the SAME run targeting one repo both acquire it (no sibling-lane serialization); AND (b) the injection merge step (`units.push(injectedUnits)`, ~L617) adds the injected unit WITHOUT deduping against a discovery unit already present for that repo this round. So injection is a backdoor to UNGUARDED intra-repo parallelism — the very thing id:ca87 says needs sub-repo claim granularity + single-owner serialized integration before it's safe. **Fix options:** (a) cheap/correct — dedupe units per repo per round at the merge step: if an injected unit's repo already has a discovery unit this round, either MERGE them into one unit (prefer the injection's verdict/prompt) or DEFER the injection to a later round (honors the one-unit-per-repo invariant; the injection is already consumed from inject.d so it must be re-enqueued, not dropped); (b) make `claim.sh acquire` NON-re-entrant within a run for distinct units (unit-id-keyed sub-lease) so sibling lanes serialize; (c) full id:ca87 intra-repo parallelism (sub-repo path-set leases + serialized single-owner merge) so same-repo units are genuinely safe to run concurrently. (a) is the immediate bleed-stop; (c) is the durable design. Severity moderate (token waste + handback noise, not data loss). Relates to id:ca87 (intra-repo parallelism safety), id:baf1 (injection path), id:ebfb (per-repo lease — note the same-run re-entrancy), id:6e9d (mid-round inject), id:719e (DMAIC: handback rework = waste). <!-- id:0547 -->
- [ ] **Light/incremental handoff for already-onboarded repos — full C1–C5 handoff is overkill** — user 2026-06-16. The `handoff` verdict (discovery classifier) fires when ROADMAP.md is missing OR every item is ticked while untracked new work exists; `references/handoff.md` then runs the full onboarding: C1 docs (CLAUDE.md/README) → C2 roadmap → C3 red tests → C4 BDD → C5 optional HARD. For a repo that's ALREADY onboarded (has CLAUDE.md, a ROADMAP.md with the marker, a test suite + BDD), re-running C1/C4 is redundant re-scaffolding — and handoff children are STRONG-model (Opus), so it's wasted Opus $ (cf. the relay-econ cost lens, id:1a75: ~71% of spend is Opus work). The common onboarded-repo trigger is the "all items ticked + untracked new work" branch — that repo doesn't need docs/BDD rebuilt, it needs the NEW work specced. WANTED: a LIGHT handoff path that detects existing scaffolding (CLAUDE.md present, ROADMAP has the marker, tests/ dir exists) and does only the INCREMENTAL work — qualify+spec the untracked new work as C2 roadmap items + C3 red tests, skip C1 docs and C4 BDD that already exist (verify, don't rewrite). Decide shape: (a) a branch inside handoff.md ("if already onboarded → incremental: C2/C3 for new work only, verify C1/C4 exist"), or (b) a distinct verdict between `handoff` and `execute` (e.g. `respec`). Note this overlaps `review` §5b reverse-handoff (which qualifies+sizes unqualified TODO/ROADMAP additions) — maybe the onboarded-repo "all-ticked + new work" case should route to a review-like reverse-handoff rather than full handoff. Relates to the discovery classifier handoff trigger, review.md §5b, id:1a75 (handoff cost). <!-- id:b14a -->

- [ ] [INPUT — meeting] **[HUMAN] Encode "ROUTINE requires the test to gate the REAL goal" in the executor scope guard** — surfaced 2026-06-16 (toesnail /relay human, mirror fidelity id:0e63). The relay's `[ROUTINE]` (Sonnet-safe) vs `[HARD]`/human split implicitly assumes **tests-are-the-spec**; that breaks when part of the success criterion lives OUTSIDE the test (semantic fidelity, faithfulness, meaning, owner judgment). Concrete case: a `.mw` mirror shipped an UNFAITHFUL transcription yet its test was GREEN, because `.mw` keys DAG edges on regex symbol refs — green for faithful AND unfaithful RHS alike. An executor gated on "test passes" would re-ship green-but-wrong work. **Rule to add** to `references/conventions.md` (executor-contract block) and the handoff/review classification step: *before tagging a tooling item `[ROUTINE]`, ask "could this test be GREEN while the actual goal is wrong?" If yes (regex/structural/schema-shape/"it parses"/"it renders" checks guarding a semantic goal) → `[HARD]` + owner/strong re-confirm.* **Tagged [HUMAN] not [ROUTINE] — self-consistently:** this is a CONTRACT change governing ~36 repos with broad behavioral consequence and NO test gating its wording; the owner ratifies it (likely a `/meeting` — overlaps the rigor-bar meeting id:80d7 and the test-integrity sanity-check id:7b4d). Relates to id:80d7, id:7b4d, review.md §2 (anti-gaming). <!-- id:33c2 -->

- [ ] **MEETING-candidate: git-notes flag for un-runnable/sanity-violated commits → `git bisect` auto-skip** — user 2026-06-16 (side-note off toesnail mirror-fidelity thread). Idea: record a per-commit signal in git notes so a `git bisect run` wrapper auto-`125`s (skips) commits that can't be meaningfully tested, and so a stale-test/sanity-violated commit is marked. **Crucial nuance the user raised (the design hinge):** bisect runs the CURRENT/uncommitted test (the bug repro) against OLD source — it preserves untracked working-tree files across checkouts and `git bisect run <script>` lives outside the tree — so a "commit X gamed its OWN committed tests" flag is largely ORTHOGONAL to bisectability (bisect may never run X's tests). The signal that genuinely pays off is **runnability**: "this commit doesn't build / the harness can't execute here" → skip. The sanity-violation flag feeds bisect only insofar as a violation made the commit un-testable. **Substrate already exists:** the verify commit-hook writes ephemeral notes on `refs/notes/verify` (`status:pending findings:…`, toesnail id:8757) and `gaming-scan.sh` (id:fa05) is the mechanical sanity detector — a bisect-skip consumer is a natural extension. **Design qs for the meeting:** (a) carrier — extend `refs/notes/verify` with a `runnable:false`/`bisect_skip:true` field vs a dedicated `refs/notes/bisect-skip` ref (a new field bumps the just-FROZEN verify schema `{status,findings}`+`{triaged,processed,verdict,review_me}` — toesnail /relay human 2026-06-16, so it's a deliberate extension not a free add); (b) who writes it (the post-commit HARD tier? gaming-scan? a separate build-probe?) and when a commit is deemed un-runnable; (c) the `git bisect run` wrapper that reads the note and returns 125; (d) notes are local-only + lossy-on-rebase (toesnail D-decisions) — acceptable for a bisect aid, or does it need durability; (e) cross-repo vs per-repo. Likely ONE `/meeting`. Relates to toesnail verify-hook cluster (id:8757/d5f9/0e63), gaming-scan.sh (id:fa05), review.md §2, id:7b4d (periodic sanity-check), id:80d7 (rigor bar). <!-- id:872e -->

- [ ] **[skeleton L4] unitPrompt guardrail trim: de-duplicate inline rules against the loaded contract** — **EVALUATED 2026-06-18, DEFERRED as low-ROI + high-blast-radius.** `unitPrompt` fires on WORK dispatches (opus review/hard, sonnet execute) whose token cost is dominated by the actual work — the ~40-line skeleton is a negligible fraction, so trimming saves little. AND it touches the UNIVERSAL child contract: inline 'NEVER push/tag/diary' + lease rules apply to ALL verdicts, but review/handoff/hard load review.md/handoff.md (NOT executor-contract.md) — moving a rule into the wrong loaded file silently drops it for some verdict (catastrophic). Wants a canary/before-after + focused session, not an AFK trim. **Blocker cleared 2026-07-01 (shardPrompt DELETED, id:a0b6) — no longer 'pending shard-prompt work'; stays DEFERRED on intrinsic low-ROI + high-blast-radius grounds.** Not a haiku/target-drift concern (work agents are sonnet/opus). See 2026-06-18-0727-relay-skeleton-token-reduction.md. <!-- id:2895 -->

- [ ] **Re-point proxy spike (id:e905) trigger to chidiAI model-degradation test** — throwaway localhost pass-through proxy (originally from 2026-06-03 meeting, living in `docs/meeting-notes/2026-06-03-1452-llm-proxy-token-ctx-and-persona-split.md`) is deferred and now explicitly gated on the chidiAI model-degradation test (WIP). Reuse that harness as the spike vehicle if/when it fires. The proxy is a **measurement/observation instrument — it reduces ZERO billed skeleton tokens** (can't beat Anthropic 0.1× server-side caching; can't cache across distinct subagent conversations; shared `ANTHROPIC_BASE_URL` blocks per-subagent routing; mutation proxy trips ToS). Must NOT be counted as a token-reduction lever. When updating id:e905: embed the chidiAI cross-link. See `docs/meeting-notes/2026-06-18-0727-relay-skeleton-token-reduction.md`. <!-- id:e905 -->

- [ ] [INPUT — meeting] **Relay broker: stop spawning one agent per mechanical shell command (WALL-TIME driver)** — user 2026-07-17, "all the Haiku agents waste so much wall time for basically mechanical tasks — I guess we should tackle the broker approach soon". MEASURED on run `relay-20260717-100452-13146` (`wf_5f223a67-ed2`, `/relay --intensive .` on loderite, 3 rounds, 30.6 min wall for ONE repo): 25 agents, of which only **4 did work** (1 sonnet execute, 1 fable review, 2 sonnet integrators) and **18 were haiku scaffolding** — 6× "run EXACTLY this one command", 3× discovery prelude, 3× discovery runner, 3× heartbeat refresh, plus quota-gate / `inject.sh take` / reconcile-on-restart / gaming-flags-log (~6 per round × 3 rounds). ROOT CONSTRAINT: the Workflow sandbox has **no shell, no filesystem, no Node API** — `agent()` is the ONLY shell escape hatch, so every `quota-stop.sh` / heartbeat / `inject.sh take` costs a full agent spawn: context load + model round-trip, **serialized on the critical path**. The 21 haiku agents burned 5.1M cache-read tokens ≈ **244k cached tokens EACH just to run one command**. NOTE THE FRAMING: this is a **wall-time** item, not a cost item — cost-wise the haiku scaffolding is minor (~7%) next to the single fable review child's 13.2M cache reads (~80%), and the user has explicitly said **the fable review is fine**; do NOT re-litigate it as a cost optimization. Corroborating prior measurement: `relay-econ.py` (id:08a3) already found across 36 runs that "status+scaffold are a bigger share of *wall-clock* than of *cost* (low concurrency → on the critical path)" — this run is a clean single-repo instance of exactly that. DIRECTION (design, NOT settled — this is why it is meeting-lane): a persistent local daemon executing the mechanical commands; precedent is the `/meeting` broker (`meeting/broker.py`, `broker-curl.sh`, `meeting-broker.service` — HTTP daemon, lazy-connect, idle-shutdown, port via `broker.json`), though that one exists to feed a renderer, not to execute commands. OPEN Q the design must answer: the workflow sandbox cannot `curl` either, so a broker still needs ≥1 agent hop per round — is the win (a) BATCHING all of a round's mechanical commands into ONE agent hop, (b) a genuinely persistent broker-client, or (c) collapsing rounds so fewer hops are needed? Also fold in the existing `echo-runner` agent type (the 2026-07-02 "relay-loop token-trim experiment" — a minimal Bash-only runner) as prior art on trimming per-hop context. Relates: id:08a3 (econ/wall-clock lens), id:c8b6 (event log), id:8419 (cheap interim), id:4416 (labels needed to measure any of this). <!-- id:3a1c -->

- [ ] **`journal.jsonl` records no labels — per-agent cost/wall attribution needs a hand-join** — user 2026-07-17, surfaced while measuring id:3a1c. A workflow's `journal.jsonl` line is only `{"type":"started|result","key":"v2:<sha>","agentId":"<id>"}` — **no `label`, no `model`, no `phase`, no prompt summary** — even though `relay-loop.js` passes `label`/`phase`/`model` to `agent()`. Consequence: answering "what did these 22 agents DO?" required joining `agent-<id>.meta.json` (has `model`, but empty `label`/`phase`) against the first user message inside each `agent-<id>.jsonl` to recover the prompt — a manual reconstruction, per run, to get facts the harness already had at spawn time. The Workflow tool's own diagnostics advertise the journal as the place to look ("one `{"type":"result",...}` line per completed agent with its full return value"), so this is a real gap in the documented path, not just an inconvenience. WANTED: persist `label`, `phase`, `model`, and a prompt digest on the `started` line (and duration/token counts on `result` if available). Note the likely split: `agent-*.meta.json` carrying `model` but EMPTY `label`/`phase` suggests the loss may be harness-side rather than relay-side — **establish which before designing a fix**; if harness-side, the relay-side fallback is to `log()` a label→agentId map per dispatch. Unblocks id:3a1c (can't quantify scaffold wall-time share per category without it) and sharpens `relay-econ.py` (id:08a3), which today re-derives categories heuristically. <!-- id:4416 -->

- [ ] **Single-repo scope: collapse per-round prelude + discovery runner + heartbeat into one agent hop** — 2026-07-17, cheap interim for id:3a1c (do NOT let this pre-empt the broker design; it is the do-now slice if the broker meeting slips). Under `args.onlyRepo` (id:7633) the discovery fan-out is already capped to 1 shard, but the round still spends SEPARATE agent hops on the prelude, the single discovery runner, and the heartbeat refresh — three serialized context loads to do what is, for one repo, one shell script's worth of work. Measured on `relay-20260717-100452-13146`: 3 rounds × ~6 scaffold agents = 18; collapsing prelude+runner+heartbeat would cut ~6–9 of them outright. IMPORTANT SCOPE NOTE: this overhead ratio is a **single-repo artifact** — on a 40-repo fleet run those same ~6 scaffold agents/round amortize across every repo, so this is NOT evidence the fleet design is wrong; the fix should be gated on `onlyRepo` being set and must not regress the fleet path. Gated on id:4416 only insofar as measuring the win needs labels. <!-- id:8419 -->

- [ ] **Collect failure reasons across relay children into a structured, queryable record (general failure ledger)** — user 2026-06-17. Today a unit's failure/handback reason lives only in the transient REPORT field and the RELAY_STATUS HANDBACK line for that run; there's no durable, aggregated record of WHY relay work fails over time. WANTED: a structured failure ledger that captures, per failed/handed-back unit, a categorized reason (e.g. `dirty-tree-race` id:0547, `gated-HARD-too-large` id:2d20, `interactive-auth-needed` id:a505, `Fable-unavailable`, `test-red`, `merge-conflict`, `quota-deferred`, `missing-dep`, `size-out`) plus repo/mode/model/run-id/timestamp — so recurring failure classes are visible and prioritizable (the DMAIC "Measure" substrate, cf. id:719e) instead of rediscovered run-by-run. Substrate already exists: the append-only `~/.config/relay/relay-events.jsonl` (id:c8b6) records dispatch/integrate/handback events — this likely extends the handback event with a `reason_category` + free-text, and adds a small reporter (`relay-failures.sh report` akin to `relay-burn.sh`/`relay-econ.py`) to roll them up by category/repo/time. Design qs: (a) closed enumeration of categories vs free-text + post-hoc clustering; (b) who classifies (the child self-reports a category in its REPORT schema vs the integrator infers from the handback reason); (c) reporter output + whether it feeds RELAY_STATUS / `/relay status` (id:ec9a) / the statusline. Pairs with id:a505 (auth-queue is one failure class) and id:719e (DMAIC waste/defect reduction). Relates to id:c8b6 (event log), id:08a3 (econ), id:2d20/id:0547 (specific failure modes). <!-- id:194e -->

- [ ] **BUG: /meeting (Opus) skipped two flow steps when invoked with a pre-formed subject arg** — observed 2026-06-16 (trAIdBTC id:abbf promotion meeting, routed in from `/relay human` which called the Skill tool with a long fully-formed subject string). The skill should, for a subject-mode meeting, proactively scan the registry (esp. personas previously introduced *in this project*) and onboard topic-relevant ad-hoc lenses in the opening exchange, not wait to be prompted. **(2) Decision options not emitted in the SAME turn as the transcript.** `format.md` §Interactive default protocol (Sonnet/Opus/Haiku) is explicit: emit the transcript chunk AND call `AskUserQuestion` in the same response — "never end a turn on bare prose and send the question in a subsequent turn." - [ ] **Persona duplication vs. name-reuse: investigation + prevention** — `append.sh -t personas` is append-only with no collision detection; re-onboarding an existing persona creates a duplicate entry (observed 2026-06-18: two Dex entries after toesnail/veq-macro-verify-carrier meeting). Design: (a) **detection** — at meeting end step 5 (save to registry), grep personas.md for the exact name before calling `append.sh` and surface a "this name already exists — merge or new name?" prompt; (b) **merge path** — a separate `append.sh update-persona <name> <new-text>` subcommand (or `Edit` on the resolved symlink path) for extending an existing entry in-place; (c) **name-collision check at meeting start** — when an ad-hoc persona is introduced, warn if their name already exists in the registry so the facilitator can re-onboard the prior persona instead of creating a fresh one. Convention: extend (same name, append lens) when the core role/domain is the same; split (new name) when the lens would confuse a future reader. <!-- id:d44d -->

## Caude statusbar

- [ ] **Statusbar: other cost-saving indicators** — ~~current session input-token running total~~ done (id:2520 — shows `<pct>%(<tokens>)` in context segment); remaining candidates: cache_read vs uncached ratio (shows caching effectiveness), model currently active. <!-- id:f394 -->
- [ ] **Statusline writes a per-session model-readable state file (let the model self-read its own ctx %, cost, quota)** — motivation 2026-06-19: the statusline RECEIVES the exact live `context_window.{total_input_tokens, total_output_tokens, context_window_size}` (+ cost + 5h/7d utilization) on stdin each render, but the MODEL never gets that object in its context — so I could not answer "what's my ctx %?" without deferring to the human's statusbar (the data exists, the model just can't see it). FIX: have `statusline/statusline-command.sh` ALSO atomically write a tiny per-session JSON (e.g. `/tmp/claude-ctx-<session_id>.json`, tmp+`mv`) on each render, keyed by the **session id from the stdin JSON** (`.session_id` — the statusline doesn't parse it today, only `.transcript_path`; add it) so the model can read it back via its own `$CLAUDE_SESSION_ID` (a stable key both sides agree on). Content: `context_pct`, `total_tokens`, `context_window_size`, `cost_usd`, `five_hour`/`seven_day`/`seven_day_sonnet` utilization, `model`, `ts`. Then the model can `cat /tmp/claude-ctx-$CLAUDE_SESSION_ID.json` to self-measure ctx/budget and decide when to `/clear` or wind down — closing the gap hit this session. Design qs: (a) path/namespace (`/tmp` like the other statusline caches, vs `$XDG_RUNTIME_DIR`) + prune stale files (mtime-based, like the usage-lock cleanup); (b) write-every-render is cheap (small JSON, atomic) but confirm no perf hit / lock contention with the existing `/tmp/claude-usage-*` writes; (c) whether to fold this into the existing usage-cache write rather than a 2nd file; (d) document the path + schema so any skill (not just the model ad-hoc) can consume it (e.g. a `/ctx` helper, or git-diary-workflow gating a wrap-up on ctx%). Cheap, additive, purely local. Relates id:2520 (context segment), the `/tmp/claude-usage-cache.json` pattern, and [[usage-on-disk-token-accounting]]. <!-- id:81cb -->
- [ ] **Quota sampler shipped — let it run, then re-evaluate** — `tools/quota-sample.sh` + `quota-sample.{service,timer}` (15-min systemd user timer) + `tools/quota-report.py` + `make install-quota-timer` SHIPPED + installed 2026-06-19 (covered by tests/test_quota_sample.sh, suite green). Motivation: the 2026-06-18 Anthropic weekly-limit accounting bug (~3% Max/Pro users, 60%→100% with no active session, acknowledged + reset same day; GH #69419/#69430/#69433) was invisible locally — the statusline only fetches `/api/oauth/usage` while a session renders it, and relay-burn.sh only samples at quota gates, so an idle spike leaves no trace. The sampler cooperates with the statusline's `/tmp/claude-usage-*` cache (reuse-if-fresh = 0 added API calls during sessions; self-fetch under the SHARED lock+backoff only when idle), writes a git-versioned JSONL to `~/src/claude-diary/quota/`. **Follow-ups (re-evaluate after it captures ≥1 real spike, or a week):** (a) optionally surface `quota-report.py` jump-alerts somewhere active (RELAY_STATUS / a notification / statusline `?` marker) instead of pull-only; (b) consider a tiny plot (matplotlib/svg) for the "later visualization" goal beyond the ASCII sparkline; (c) decide whether relay-burn.sh should read these idle samples too (richer burnup substrate, cf. id:219b/id:c8b6). Verified locally: cooperative cache-read + scoped diary commit both land. <!-- id:d267 -->
- [ ] **Quota gate must LOUDLY surface a requested-but-unenforceable weekly cap instead of silently gating on a zero** (user 2026-07-10) — `seven_day.utilization` reads **0.0 on a fresh cache** while `.limits[]` `weekly_all.is_active=false`, so `--quota-7d`/`RELAY_QUOTA_THRESHOLD_SEVEN_DAY` cannot bind — only `five_hour` actually guards a pool. Evidence (`~/src/claude-diary/quota/quota-samples.jsonl`): `seven_day` climbed **27%→33% across 2026-07-08**, then reads **0.0 on 2026-07-10 within the SAME weekly window** (resets 2026-07-14) — utilization cannot fall mid-window, so the 0.0 is a non-report, not a real drop. Consequence: a run that passes `--quota-7d 45` gets NO 7-day protection yet `quota-stop.sh` treats the absent/zeroed bucket as "well under cap" and proceeds silently. **FIX:** at the quota gate, detect a non-reporting / inactive weekly bucket (`seven_day.utilization` null-or-0 **and** the corresponding `.limits[]` `weekly_all.is_active=false`) and, **only when a 7-day cap was explicitly requested** (`--quota-7d` / `RELAY_QUOTA_THRESHOLD_SEVEN_DAY` set), LOUDLY surface "requested 7-day cap is currently unenforceable (weekly bucket not reporting)" rather than silently gating on the zero (id:4347 no-silent-swallow). Do NOT hard-stop on it (observe-first) and do NOT touch the tested absent-bucket skip fail-safes (id:c5ba/id:0175) — this is an additive LOUD notice on the *requested-but-dead* path. Cross-ref memory `usage-api-per-model-weekly-null-2026-06-30`; relates the id:d267 sampler (evidence source) and the front-door `--quota-7d` mapping (SKILL.md). <!-- id:c471 -->
- [ ] **Claude Code TUI: ghost workflow-progress + duplicate-statusline fragments bleed into the prompt after exiting `/workflows` while a background workflow keeps emitting progress** — observed 2026-06-22 (both with and WITHOUT tmux): orphaned fragments persist on the main REPL prompt — the workflow progress-group header (`○relay-loop  Priority-mixed 5-wide…`), stray run-progress counters (`8`, `67`, `2 43`), and a DUPLICATE relay statusline segment (e.g. `KV:07:30  🔁2 ✓4 ⊙0`) on a second line. Purely cosmetic (shell/git/session state intact); `Ctrl+L` or a terminal resize (SIGWINCH) clears it. Root cause (per claude-code-guide investigation): a render RACE between the background-task progress writer and the TUI's line-clear/cursor-position logic when repainting the prompt after leaving the full-screen panel — the panel exit doesn't halt the concurrent progress writer. **Status: KNOWN-OPEN upstream**, same family as GH [anthropics/claude-code#19894](https://github.com/anthropics/claude-code/issues/19894) (stale background-task count; closed-as-duplicate → tracked internally) and the fullscreen-corruption fixes in changelog **v2.1.181** ("statusline mid-screen, duplicated spinner rows, merged text … under heavy nested-subagent load") + v2.1.152 (simplified Workflow inline progress). **#1 ACTION: this box runs Claude Code 2.1.177, which PREDATES v2.1.181 — upgrade to latest and retest; likely fixed or reduced.** Mitigations: `"disableWorkflows": true` (settings.json / `CLAUDE_CODE_DISABLE_WORKFLOWS=1`) removes the race — but **UNSUITABLE here** since the relay pool DEPENDS on the Workflow tool, so do NOT set it; workable fallback is discipline — exit `/workflows` (Esc) and wait for the footer to show **0 background agents/workflows** before resuming REPL. statusline refresh throttle (300 ms / 2 s) is not user-configurable and wouldn't help (logic race, not throughput). If it persists after upgrade, file a new issue citing #19894 + repro (launch a long `/relay` workflow → `/workflows` → Esc while it's still updating → ghost fragments on the prompt). External/harness bug, not repo code — tracked here as a meta-issue. <!-- id:f576 -->
- [ ] **Investigate the statusline cost figure vs raw list-price API cost (~2× gap)** — observed 2026-06-26 in a kienzler-homepage session (Opus 4.8): the statusline `💸` cost read **~$8.10**, then **$12.89** later in the same session, while an independent recompute from the transcript via `~/.claude/skills/meeting/cost-of.sh` + Opus 4.8 list pricing (in $5 / out $25 / cache-read $0.50 / cache-write-5m $6.25 per MTok) came to **≈$16.70** (cache-read dominated: ~18.4M cache-read tokens). The two disagree by ~2×. Hypothesis: the statusline reports a **subscription-effective / amortised** rate (Max-plan / fast-mode), not pay-as-you-go list price — but this is unconfirmed. **Action:** (a) find where `statusline/statusline-command.sh` sources the cost number (the `/api/oauth/usage` object on stdin? a `cost_usd` field? a local multiplier?); (b) determine whether it's list-price or plan-effective, and document which in the statusline docs so the figure isn't mistaken for billable API spend; (c) if it IS list-price, reconcile why it undercounts cache-read-heavy sessions by ~2× (cache-tier rate applied wrong? output-only?); (d) consider exposing both numbers or a tooltip/legend. Relates the id:81cb model-readable state-file (same cost source) and `cost-of.sh`. <!-- id:ad9d -->

## worktrees / D-series

- [ ] **Nothing stops an executor child and its supervisor from running `make test` in the SAME worktree at once — and the resulting red is indistinguishable from a real one** — found 2026-07-16 during the id:7612 integration. The executor contract's done-check tells the child to run the full suite in its worktree; invariant 5 has the integrator **re-derive** that check before merging. Neither says anything about **overlap**, and the pool's lease (id:0902/ebfb) is per-REPO, not per-worktree — it does not serialize two suites inside one worktree. Observed here: the child ran `make test` and stalled waiting on it, so the supervisor ran `make test` on the same worktree concurrently → `247 passed, 1 failed`. Once the child's run ended the same command passed **3/3** (248/0, 248/0, 249/0). The failing assertion was a `grep` for a call site in a static file — which cannot vary unless something rewrote it mid-run — so **the mechanism is NOT established** and is deliberately not claimed; the correlation is 5 data points with no counterexample. **Why it matters:** a contaminated red is not just noise — it is *evidence-shaped*. It blocked a merge (conservative, fine) but sent the reviewer hunting `SRC_DIR`, `export DEST_DIR`, the `lint` prereq and stashing tests for a phantom, and it produced a confidently-wrong "deterministic, not flaky" verdict to the owner (chidiai case `2026-07-16-determinism-asserted-over-self-created-confound`). A red that means nothing costs more than no signal at all. **Fix candidates:** (a) **establish the mechanism first** — reproduce two concurrent suites in one worktree and find what actually varies (an observe-first spike; if nothing does, the correlation is wrong and this item dissolves); (b) a per-worktree test lock (`flock` on `<worktree>/.make-test.lock`) so a second suite waits rather than interleaves; (c) contract rule — the integrator does NOT re-run the suite while the child's own run may be live (needs a liveness signal the supervisor can read: the child's stall is currently only visible as prose in its final message); (d) cheapest and maybe sufficient — have the child report its suite result and the integrator re-derive **only after** confirming no live run (`pgrep`), treating a red under concurrency as UNKNOWN rather than FAIL. Prefer (a) before building any of (b)–(d) — [[observe before preventing]]. Relates id:0902/ebfb (per-repo lease), id:7612, the executor contract done-check, and [[mechanize-reliab]]. <!-- id:93bd -->

- [ ] **Nothing detects an uninstalled canonical script — 5 were missing symlinks, incl. the id:f682 isolation gate** — found 2026-07-16. Skills install as per-file symlinks, so a newly-added canonical script needs a `make install-<skill>` run to appear in `~/.claude/skills/`. Five relay scripts had **no symlink** and were silently absent at call time: `worktree-retire.sh` + `verify-isolation.sh` + `handback-guard.mjs` + `mechanical-orphan-scan.sh` + `mechanical-orphan-draft.sh` (57 installed vs 63 canonical). `verify-isolation.sh` is the **safety gate SKILL.md invariant 5 mandates** (id:f682 — aborts a merge when a child wrote to the main checkout instead of its worktree); it was uninstalled, i.e. the documented gate could not have been running. `worktree-retire.sh` (added 07-15 for id:373e) was likewise never installed, so integrator step 5 was calling a nonexistent path. **Refined 2026-07-16 after investigation — the manifests were NEVER the problem:** `git log -S'verify-isolation' -- Makefile` returns exactly one commit (`05042a4`), the same one that added the script, and it registered it in `relay_FILES`/`relay_EXEC`/`relay_ALLOW` simultaneously. So this is the milder finding: `make install-relay` simply wasn't re-run for ~21h, NOT a manifest omission that made installation impossible. **The drift is two-surfaced, though** — the same staleness hit the **allowlist**: `worktree-retire.sh` and `verify-isolation.sh` were in `relay_ALLOW` but had **0** entries in `~/.claude/settings.json` (vs 8 for `ckpt-tag.sh`) because `make install-allowlist` hadn't been run either. An un-allowlisted helper prompts, and an unattended pool cannot answer a prompt — so allowlist drift silently degrades the pool exactly like symlink drift does. Both fixed this session (`make install-relay` + `make install-allowlist`; 16 narrow script-scoped entries added, `rm -f`/`-rf` ask-guards untouched). The **class** is still unfixed: `make status` reports skill-level symlink state, and nothing fails when a canonical script has no installed counterpart — the failure surfaces only as a runtime "command not found" inside an agent, where it is easy to miss. **Fix candidates:** (a) a test that diffs canonical `relay/scripts/*` against `~/.claude/skills/relay/scripts/*` and fails on drift (generalize per-skill; skip `__pycache__`); (b) extend `make status` to report per-file drift, not just skill-level; (c) have `relay-doctor.sh` check that every script the loop invokes actually resolves (it already checks reference-doc install completeness, id:69ef — same shape); (d) make a missing helper a LOUD failure at call site rather than a silent skip; (e) **cover the allowlist surface too** — assert every `<skill>_ALLOW` script has its 8 entries in the live `settings.json`, else the pool prompts and stalls unattended. Note (a)/(b) are the cheap mechanical wins; both drift surfaces share one root — *the manifest is the SSOT but nothing verifies the installed artifact matches it*. Relates id:69ef (reference-doc install check), id:373e, id:f682, id:7612 (the gate that isn't wired at all — a superset problem: installing a script nothing calls fixes nothing). <!-- id:c5ed -->

- [ ] **AI-4 (worktree TODO.md scope)** — after ≥1 live `/meeting` run from a `meeting-rpg` worktree, log whether autonomous upward traversal of TODO.md recurs. If yes, escalate to mechanical guard design (D5 follow-up). See: `docs/meeting-notes/2026-05-20-2105-todo-md-root-resolution-worktrees.md`. <!-- id:3507 -->

- [ ] **D6 — sub-agent parallel Class 1 dispatcher (build-gated)** — design recorded 2026-06-04. Gate: **(1) D5 ratified ✓ 2026-06-04**, (2) ≥3 independent disjoint-footprint items logged at once, **(3) Haiku-vs-Sonnet pilot ✓ 2026-06-04** — Sonnet-default confirmed. ## hooks / commit safety

- [ ] **`git-lock-push.sh` manifest mode silently no-ops against a chronically-dirty repo** — discovered 2026-06-19 building the quota sampler (id:d267): a manifest-mode call (`-f <file> -m <msg>`) on `~/src/claude-diary` (which is ~always dirty — DIARY.md edits in flight) **committed nothing yet returned exit 0**, so the caller logged "committed+pushed" while the file stayed untracked. Two compounding causes: (1) manifest mode stages+commits the listed paths (line 85) but then hits the **id:aa93 dirty-tree refusal** (line 123, the *other* unstaged files) and exits 0 non-fatally — yet in the observed run the listed-path commit ALSO didn't land (needs root-cause: is `git commit` partial-staging the manifest paths, or does an empty/failed stage slip through `set -e`?); (2) nesting matters — a caller already holding an flock on the repo's `.git-lock-push.lock` (fd 8) cannot call git-lock-push (it `exec 8>`s the same file → 30s deadlock). **Impact:** any automation trying to auto-commit ONE scoped file into a repo that carries unrelated dirty state can silently lose the commit while believing it succeeded. The sampler worked around it with an explicit scoped partial commit (`git commit -- <path>`) under the lock + opportunistic clean-tree-only push (see `tools/quota-sample.sh` §3). **Fix candidates:** (a) make manifest mode return NON-zero (or a distinct code) when the intended paths didn't actually commit, so callers can't false-log success; (b) document that manifest mode requires an otherwise-clean tree and is unsuitable for chronically-dirty repos; (c) offer a `--scoped-commit-only` mode that commits the listed paths and SKIPS the rebase/push when the rest of the tree is dirty (what the sampler reimplemented); (d) note the fd-8 self-nesting deadlock in the script header. Relates [[id:aa93 dirty-tree guard]], id:d267, id:3558 (worktree-per-session, the deeper fix). <!-- id:3b18 -->

- [ ] **Add a `make` target that installs the destructive-op guardrail into `settings.json`** (user 2026-07-15) — the auto-mode destructive-op guardrail (`autoMode.soft_deny` + `permissions.ask` for `rm -f`/`-rf`/`--force`, git force ops, and the destructive-non-force family `git reset --hard` / `restore` / `checkout -- ` / `clean -f`; documented in `docs/destructive-op-guardrail.md`) was added by hand to one machine's `~/.claude/settings.json` and is NOT yet in the install flow — a fresh `make install` (or a `settings.json` reset) on another machine wouldn't carry it. Add an **idempotent** `install-guardrails` (name TBD) merge target, wired into the top-level `install` target, mirroring `install-allowlist` / `install-relay-env` (which merge into `SETTINGS_JSON` via `tools/allowlist.py` / `tools/settings-env.py`). It must merge the `autoMode.soft_deny` rules (preserving `$defaults` and any existing entries) + the `permissions.ask` patterns without clobbering other settings, and be safe to re-run. Consider a source fragment (like `tools/allow-extra.txt`) for the rule set so it's reviewable/versioned here. Relates the settings-merge tooling, `docs/destructive-op-guardrail.md`. <!-- id:98fc -->

## local-llama-swap subagent delegation

- [ ] Conditional on bounded-B passing: commit a thin `curl`+`jq` local-delegation wrapper with outcome logging (task/model/outcome, zelegator-consumable) and loud-fail on n_ctx overflow. Contract: routes a bounded prompt to localhost:8080/v1, appends one log line per call, no silent truncation. See `docs/meeting-notes/2026-06-11-2235-subagents-local-llama-swap.md`. <!-- id:85d2 -->
- [ ] Forward-flags: (a) auto-routing local-vs-remote → zelegator; (b) opencode agentic-local escape hatch — **C-agentic still untested (deferred); run with 30b model in a clean-memory session before closing this flag.** See `docs/meeting-notes/2026-06-11-2300-subagents-local-llama-spike-finding.md`. <!-- id:f579 -->
- [ ] **A fourth "model" tier = MECHANICAL EXECUTION (no real LLM) for pure-transport agents.** Motivated by the a0b6 classifier flip (2026-07-01): `relay-loop.js`'s `discover-run` runner and `discover-prelude` are now pure transport — they only run a fixed script recipe per item and relay the JSON verbatim (zero reasoning). A Haiku pilot ran `discover-run` correctly in exactly 3 tool calls (one `discover-repo.sh` per repo), so Haiku is the current floor — but even Haiku spends tokens + a model round-trip for work that is deterministic. The idea: inject a fourth tier alongside opus/sonnet/haiku that the Workflow `agent()` interface dispatches to but which executes the recipe DETERMINISTICALLY (no LLM). Constraint driving it: a Workflow script is sandboxed (no `exec`/subprocess), so `agent()` is the ONLY way to shell out — hence the tier can't be "nothing", it must be a real dispatch target. Candidate mechanisms: (a) revive the local-LLM-proxy (intercept `agent()` calls tagged `mechanical` and run the recipe via a local runner, returning schema-valid JSON — the [[local-llama-subagent-architecture]] proxy shape, spike id:95e3); (b) a local MCP "recipe-runner" tool the Workflow calls instead of `agent()`; (c) a harness primitive that runs a whitelisted command list and validates against the output schema. Anti-goal: do NOT reintroduce an LLM where determinism suffices (mechanize-first). Gate/relate: needs the `agent()`-injection-point question answered (is there a non-LLM dispatch target?); the parser-vs-proxy token-accounting spike; and the ToS/out-of-harness-billing tripwire ([[hermes-deferral-contract]]). First cheap step once unblocked: measure the Haiku-vs-mechanical per-round token+latency delta on `discover-run`/`discover-prelude` to size the win. Surfaced 2026-07-01 (user) right after the flip made the first genuinely-mechanical agents. **CHARACTERIZED + DEFERRED 2026-07-01 (background research agent, user-directed pilot-first):** the tier as-specified is **NOT buildable today** — confirmed against the harness that `agent()` has **no non-LLM dispatch target**; a "tier" is just a model-string mapped to a billed Anthropic model. All three candidate mechanisms fail their guardrails: (a) proxy = the already-REJECTED [[local-llama-subagent-architecture]] shape + pool-wide `ANTHROPIC_BASE_URL` alias poisoning + [[hermes-deferral-contract]] ToS tripwire; (b) MCP recipe-runner = a Workflow script **cannot call MCP directly** (only a spawned agent can) so it still spends the LLM round-trip — defeats the anti-goal; (c) whitelisted-command primitive = **doesn't exist** (an Anthropic feature request, file via `/feedback`). Given the sizing (post-a0b6 discovery is 1–3 short agent calls/round, sig-cached to fire only on churn), a mechanical tier would be **gold-plating** vs the real, already-de-risked win — which the agent found and **LANDED**: `discover-prelude` (:733) + `discover-run` (:849) still dispatched `model:'sonnet'` despite being pure transport → flipped **both to `haiku`** (the item's own "first cheap step"). The prelude flip needed a prompt hardening (emit **ABSOLUTE** paths — a literal `~` fed to `discover-sig.sh` yields an empty fail-open sig that silently disables the discovery cache; latent fragility, not haiku-specific); **re-piloted haiku = 50/50 non-empty sigs**, discover-run pilot = 3 tool calls; `test_discover_cache.sh` D1 pin updated sonnet→haiku; suite 151/0. **REMAINING = a parked forward-flag** on a future Anthropic mechanical/tool-runner dispatch primitive (`/feedback` filed if pursued); not executor-pickable. Measure residual haiku discovery cost only if it looks material after the flip. <!-- id:2ec4 -->

- [ ] **[TRIGGER-GATED] Wholesale off-Workflow discovery investigation** (D4) — reimplement worktrees/leases/integrator/quota-stop outside the Workflow (zero LLM anywhere, own the parallelism). Do NOT build pre-trigger. Trigger = the residual queue-read (id:7402) proving unreliable/insufficient in practice, OR the launch-wall (id:af30) staying unsolved long enough to block D3's elimination. See `docs/meeting-notes/2026-07-07-1228-relay-discovery-off-workflow.md`. <!-- id:882a -->

## Fable review 2026-07-08 — relay mechanization (verified findings; full trail in the 2026-07-08 diary entry)

- [ ] [HARD] ** mechanical-daemon hardening: running/ reaper, `.timer` retry companion, flock, wall-clock timeout, resource ACQUIRE not probe, single resource vocabulary, loud inject-failure** (Fable review 2026-07-08) — verified against `mechanical-daemon.sh`: (1) daemon death between `:109` (mv→running) and `:111` strands the recipe in `running/` FOREVER — no code anywhere scans running/ (recipe-manifest.md promises it's a recoverable marker; nothing delivers); add a startup-tick reaper (stale running/ → surfaced/requeued LOUDLY); (2) the only trigger is edge-based (`mechanical-daemon.path` PathModified on pending/) — a DEFERRED recipe doesn't modify pending/, so the documented "retried next tick" is actually "stalls until an unrelated write"; add a `.timer` companion; (3) no flock — a manual `run` racing the `.path`-fired service makes the loser's `mv` fail and abort the whole tick mid-batch under `set -e`; (4) `est_wall` gates launch but `bash -c` at `:110` has NO `timeout` — a hung cmd holds the oneshot active and blocks every future tick; wrap in `timeout <est_wall×k>`; (5) `:102` only PROBES the resource claim, never ACQUIRES it — two recipes (or recipe + concurrent pool job) both see "free" and launch together on one GPU; acquire via claim.sh for the run duration (relates the id:33d3 claim-liveness work); (6) `relay-intensity.sh:49` and `resource-probe.sh:35` disagree on the resource vocabulary and `recipe-validate.sh` checks against neither → a plausible `resource:"llama"` recipe defers FOREVER as resource-unavailable — a silent-forever-defer (id:4347 class); one vocab source, validate at intake; (7) inject failure after a successful run is a log-line swallow (`:114-116`) — a completed mechanical run never gets reviewed; escalate via the decision-queue (id:de31), never log-and-continue. TRUST BOUNDARY (meeting lane — folded into id:d0c0/ec23): `bash -c` runs recipe cmds verbatim as the user and the "only relay writes pending/" invariant is documented, not enforced (plain user-writable dir + auto-fire `.path`). <!-- id:1cb8 -->

- [ ] **Make `--all` explicit across ALL relay subcommands — bare invocation = cwd repo only** (user 2026-06-15) — `review` and `next` already default to the cwd repo (`git rev-parse --show-toplevel`) and require `--all`/a repo-list for the cross-repo sweep (the historical default-flip), but `human` and `handoff` still default to "all confirmed own repos".   - **id:2909 MEETING HELD 2026-06-15** (`docs/meeting-notes/2026-06-15-1610-adversarial-review-anti-gaming.md`). Decisions: defer the plural refuter fleet (zero recorded gaming incidents — observe-before-preventing); build gaming-canary corpus (two tiers: Tier A bash + Tier B model harness); extract mechanical checks to `gaming-scan.sh`; flag-rate logger to `~/.claude/logs/relay-gaming-flags.log`.   - **Implementation shape when the fleet IS built — `ultracode`-style adversarial sub-workflow, NOT a blanket relay mode** (noted 2026-06-29). Asked whether `ultracode` (the "author a Workflow per task, adversarially verify everything, token cost no constraint" standing mode) belongs in /relay. Verdict: NO as a blanket mode — the relay is quota-bound, and its whole token-economy history (discover Opus→sonnet 35% leak, "discover=47.6% of cost" lever, integrator-batching, 46%-agents-Haiku-overhead audit) is the exact opposite of "cost no constraint"; importing it wholesale regresses that work. AND the relay already cherry-picked the good ultracode patterns where they pay (review = adversarial verify + gaming-scan + test-diff-vs-checkpoint; drain detector = loop-until-dry; parallel discover shards = multi-modal fan-out). The ONE high-value targeted slice is exactly THIS deferred fleet: when built, wire a small `parallel()` 2–3-voter refute panel into REVIEW MODE ONLY, fired solely on a non-empty `gaming_flags` (the `// DEFERRED-FLEET SEAM` in id:3826's spec, relay-loop.js `integrate()`), behind this item's flag-rate evidence gate — never per-unit. Keeps cost where it earns its keep; consistent with mechanize-cheap/escalate-on-evidence. Folds into id:719e (DMAIC waste-vs-defect lens). Relates id:3826 (the seam + logger), id:719e.

- [ ] **Discover-speedup track (user-prioritized 2026-06-15: "discover always takes so long")** — the per-round discovery is ONE Opus agent (no `model:` override, relay-loop.js:425) sequentially scanning 30+ repos (fetch + sync-guard + worktree-reconcile/reap + classify + 8 per-repo fields) plus a global prelude (runId, `inject.sh take`, `claim.sh peek`). LLM-in-the-loop = the latency AND cost. Three composable levers, in build order: <!-- id:6788 -->
  - **(1) ✅ SHIPPED 2026-06-15 — parallel-shard the LLM scan** <!-- id:9ed4 --> (relay-loop.js: a once-only `discover-prelude` agent does runId + the consuming `inject.sh take` + `claim.sh peek` + own-repo list + non-own skipped; then N round-robin `discover-shard` classifiers fan out via `parallel(chunks.map(...))` and merge into the same discovery object. `DISCOVER_SHARDS` knob, default 6. `tests/test_relay_discover_shard.sh`, suite 44 green.) — split the per-repo classification across N cheaper agents instead of one sequential Opus pass. REQUIRES first extracting the **global prelude** (generate runId once; `inject.sh take` is *consuming* so it must run EXACTLY once; `claim.sh peek` once) out of the per-shard work, then fanning out shard agents (each given the shared runId + peek result + its repo subset), then merging `{units, surfaced, skipped}`. Biggest latency cut for least rewrite; ship first. Red test: assert the prelude (inject take / runId) runs once and discovery fans out over repo shards.
  - **(2) Incremental HEAD-keyed cache (the SAFE caching)** <!-- id:bc39 --> — cache per-repo `{HEAD, dirty-hash, claim-state}` from last round; a repo whose tuple is byte-identical reuses its cached verdict, only CHANGED repos are re-classified. Invalidation-keyed on actual git state, NOT time (this is why it's safe where id:22ef's reject-verdict-caching warning does not apply — that warned against *time/blind* caching). Skips the bulk of repeat work in steady state. Red test: a repo with unchanged HEAD/dirty/claim is not re-scanned; any change invalidates.
  - **(3) Deterministic scanner = the real fix** <!-- id:23fe --> — extend the EXISTING `scripts/discover-repos.sh` (already emits ownership/dirty/last-ckpt TSV in seconds) to emit the full verdict JSON (DISCOVER_SCHEMA): the 4 classification rules + the 3ac8 worktree reconciliation become tested shell, the LLM is left only the one irreducible NL bit (acceptable-dirt per relay.toml comment) or dropped. Removes the model from the hot path AND de-risks 3ac8's reaping into tested code. Same id as the Wiggum-agenda item. Red test: discover-repos.sh emits schema-valid verdict JSON matching the LLM classifier on a fixture repo set. **FOLD IN 2026-06-29 (user):** also emit the recurring **cheap pre-scan** fields a strong-turn `handoff&review --all` needs per confirmed `own` repo — unaudited-commit count since last ckpt, ROADMAP open-`[ ]` count, TODO open-`[ ]` count, dirty-state — **resolving repos+paths from relay.toml (honoring `# path:`), NOT a `~/src/*` glob**. This session a strong turn improvised exactly that glob scan and missed the nested `zkm/plugins/*` repos; the fix is to make the tested scanner the only path so no per-run improvisation is needed (cf. [[feedback-use-existing-tools-not-improvise]], [[feedback-mechanize-no-swallow-stderr]]).
  - **(also ✅ SHIPPED 2026-06-15) status-write off the critical path** <!-- id:cb50 --> — the Haiku `write-relay-status` agent was `await`ed between discover→dispatch and at round end, so the next discover/dispatch blocked on a pure visibility side-effect (user caught the pool sitting on just a write-relay-status when discovery could already proceed). Now `scheduleStatusWrite` snapshots the content and queues the write on a serialized `statusTail`; the pool proceeds immediately and the run flushes the tail once before returning. `tests/test_relay_status_offcrit.sh`.
  - **Build deliberately, NOT into a running pool** — discovery is the single most critical step; each lever lands with its red test, relay-loop.js edits affect only the NEXT launch, and the current pool finishes on the old code. Sequence 1→2→3 (cb50 done). <!-- id:9ed4 --> <!-- id:bc39 -->

- [ ] **[DESIGN/meeting] Connectivity-resilient relay — craft a deterministic workflow per session, then run mostly WITHOUT live cloud dependency** — **Motivation (user 2026-06-15): "that incident shows how volatile cloud-AI dependency is."** A 2-hour pool run = hundreds of live `agent()` cloud calls; a single network drop killed discover-shard:6 + a status write mid-run, and a deterministic `new Date()` bug crashed the whole pool. Every per-step cloud round-trip is a failure point. **Direction:** have the STRONG turn *craft a deterministic workflow per session* (plan/decide once, cloud-side), then *execute* it with as few live cloud `agent()` calls as possible: <!-- id:a778 -->
  - **Mechanize the mechanical steps** → tested shell, no LLM in the hot path: the deterministic `discover-repos.sh` emitting verdict JSON (id:23fe), a deterministic `relay-integrate.sh` (merge→tag→push→prune as shell, frees a slot + removes a cloud call per integration), the HEAD-keyed discovery cache (id:bc39).
  - **Local-model fallback for the irreducibly-LLM steps** when cloud is down/volatile — review/handoff judgment via a local model ([[local-llama-subagent-architecture]] B-spine; spike id:95e3 gates the wrapper). Degrade-not-die: cloud blip → fall back to local, not crash.
  - **Lean on resume** for crash/drop recovery: `Workflow({scriptPath, resumeFromRunId})` replays the cached agent prefix; pair with the relay's external-state mutation (resume-safety — fresh-relaunch vs resume tradeoff, noted 2026-06-15).
  - **Open questions** (route to a /meeting): which steps are *irreducibly* cloud-LLM vs mechanizable; the local-model quality bar for discover/review; how "craft once, run deterministically" reconciles with the pool's side-effecting git/worktree mutation; whether a session crafts ONE big workflow or the strong turn keeps emitting smaller deterministic units. Connects: id:23fe, id:95e3, the Date-crash guard (test_relay_no_date_api.sh), the failed-shard surfacing (953cf2e). <!-- id:cfa9 -->

- [ ] **Guard relay-loop.js against the pool's own Workflow-sandbox bugs** — 2026-06-15 the autonomous pool crashed/degraded THREE times from its executor/review children editing the Workflow engine (`relay-loop.js`) with code the static tests can't validate against the LIVE Workflow runtime: a partial id:8c35 (unwired), `new Date()` (id:3826, db5ec43), and `process.env.HOME` (id:3826, a8fe504) — the last two threw synchronously out of `integrate()` and killed the whole pool at the first REVIEW integration. `tests/test_relay_no_date_api.sh` now statically flags Date/process/require/fs/Math.random, but that's per-class whack-a-mole. Deeper fix: either a **runtime smoke check** ("does relay-loop.js start + run one no-op round under the Workflow shim?") gating any merge that touches it, OR treat `relay-loop.js` as a **protected file** only attended sessions edit (executors hand back relay-engine changes instead of committing them). Connects id:cfa9. <!-- id:e37b -->

- [ ] **Verify the `id:da26` remainder after the next dotclaude-skills review/executor loop** (user 2026-06-15) — the da26 "REMAINING" work (deep `-d`/flag-matrix cleanup + relay-loop.js `elevation→lowest-prio-bonus` reframe) lives as a NOTE *inside* id:da26, not its own ROADMAP line, so D6 reverse-handoff probably won't extract it. dotclaude-skills has unaudited commits → the next `/relay` WILL review it; afterwards CHECK: did reverse-handoff promote the remainder to ROADMAP and an executor/`hard` unit pick it up, or did it fall through? If it fell through, split the remainder into its own `[HARD]` ROADMAP line so the pool sees it. <!-- id:e0c1 -->

- [ ] **Octopus-merge consolidation for independent parallel worktrees finishing close in time** — when the serialized integrator has ≥2 verified worktree branches that are mutually NON-CONFLICTING and completed within a short window, consider a single `git merge --no-ff branchA branchB branchC` (octopus) → ONE integration commit + ONE checkpoint + ONE push, instead of N sequential `--no-ff` merges + N tags + N pushes. Benefits: less RELAY_LOG/tag noise, fewer pushes, faster drain. Decision-call / constraints: (a) the octopus strategy REFUSES on any conflict, so it's only valid for provably-disjoint file sets — the SAME independence test that licensed running them in parallel; (b) loses per-track checkpoint granularity (relay tags per-track today) — a single bad track can't be cherry-excluded post-merge as cleanly, so prefer sequential when any track is unverified/risky; (c) attribution: the combined ckpt message MUST enumerate each track's id + summary. Heuristic: octopus when N≥2 disjoint + each individually gate-verified + close-in-time; fall back to sequential when tracks share files or need independent checkpoints/bisect points. Observed first-hand 2026-06-17 (zkWhale demo-chain): THEME + emoji-svgs + logo were near-independent and finished within minutes — a 3-way octopus would have collapsed 3 merges/tags/pushes into one. (user request 2026-06-17) <!-- id:8691 -->
  - **Field report — zkWhale demo-chain run, 2026-06-17/18 (~20 background agents, directed `/relay --afk`):** Ran ~20 worktree children in waves of 1–3, integrated sequentially (merge → full gate → ckpt-tag → push) ≈20×. Findings: (1) **Conflicts were NOT the bottleneck** — disjoint file-scoping *in the child prompts* prevented nearly all of them; the real tax was the repeated **per-merge integration ceremony**, dominated by re-running the full gate each time (`pnpm test` ~8–15 s + typecheck + lint) plus a push apiece. Octopus's win here is halving *gate-runs + pushes* for co-ready disjoint waves, more than the tag/log noise. (2) **Octopus opportunities genuinely arose ~4–5×** (THEME+emoji-svgs; spinrot+logofix; the two logo rounds; proofglyph+badgesvg) — each ≥2 branches, file-disjoint, individually green, finished within minutes. (3) **The octopus-blockers that actually recurred were a small set of high-churn shared files:** `strings.ts` (almost every UI agent appends copy — distinct keys so git *auto-merged*, but it's the #1 risk), `package.json`/`pnpm-lock.yaml` (new devDeps: vite-plugin-singlefile, jimp, potrace), hot UI files like `ArtifactScreen.tsx` (touched by demo-mount/spinner/emphasis across waves), and the ledgers (`TODO.md`). Plus genuine **dependency chains** forced sequencing regardless of merge strategy (a8c2-wiring after the spinner work; demo-transparent-drop after demo-polish). (4) **Deterministic eligibility predictor that would've worked:** pairwise-intersect `git diff --name-only main..<branch>` across the co-ready candidates; empty intersection ⇒ octopus-safe. (5) **Granularity downside barely bit this workload** — every track was gate-verified *before* merge, so I never needed to bisect/cherry-exclude a track post-integration; a well-formed combined ckpt message preserved the attribution that per-track tags gave. (6) **Recommended impl:** optimistic octopus — `git merge --no-ff b1 b2 …` (git refuses cleanly on conflict, no half-merge), fall back to sequential for the conflicting subset; gate ONCE after the merged result; run `pnpm install` once if any branch touched the manifest (orthogonal to merge strategy but required before the gate). Net: for this run, a file-intersection-gated optimistic octopus would have cut ~5–7 of the ~20 integration cycles (~30%) with negligible downside. (field report 2026-06-18)

- [ ] **Directed `/relay <args>` front-session should spawn children as BACKGROUND agents by default** — user request 2026-06-17. A directed/scoped/`--afk` run (e.g. `/relay . --afk <directive>`) is driven by the strong front session fanning out via the Agent tool (handoff/review C4), NOT the autonomous-pool Workflow. Those Agent spawns should default to `run_in_background: true` so the session feels like the no-arg autonomous pool front-door: work happens in the background, the front session is purely the COORDINATOR (status, serialized integration, checkpoints, summaries) — the only thing surfaced in the front session is coordinator output, not blocking agent transcripts. Today this depends on the operator remembering to background each Agent call; make it the documented default in `references/handoff.md` + `references/review.md` (and the orchestrator invariants §4 "Spawn waves"). Keep foreground only when a child's result is an immediate hard dependency of the very next coordinator step. Connects id:8691 (octopus-merge integration) — together they make a directed run behave like a lightweight pool: background fan-out + consolidated integration. (user request 2026-06-17) **REINFORCED 2026-07-19 (user) + chidiai evidence — make it STRUCTURAL, not intent:** the orchestrator/foreground agent has now been chidilog'd for reaching for the full discovery+self-feeding Workflow (`relay-loop.js`) on work that warranted lean direct subagent dispatch — `chidiai 2026-07-18-launched-the-full-autonomous-discovery-self` (Moderate; invariant *Match machinery to work-size*: spun up discovery shards + the re-discovery `while` loop for a single already-specced `[ROUTINE]` item, user had to interrupt "I did not ask you to spawn a useless discovery agent spawning loop"). User ask: `/relay .` (and similar scoped/directed forms) should **MEAN** "spawn the adequate subagents for the cwd repo's already-known backlog, WITHOUT the discovery-loop Workflow" — but today the front door still resolves `.` into a `relay-loop.js` launch merely *scoped* to one repo (SKILL.md:195), so discovery shards + the self-feeding loop spin up even for one repo. **Design Qs (→ likely `[HARD — meeting]`):** (a) redefine `.`/scoped/directed invocation to bypass `relay-loop.js` entirely and fan out via background Agent spawns (this item's core) vs. add an explicit lean flag; (b) relationship to `/relay next` (lean cwd router, but current-session — it does NOT spawn background subagents) — is the wanted mode "`next` but backgrounded / multi-item"?; (c) **role-boundary constraint** from sibling `chidiai 2026-07-18-a-relay-review-sub-agent-scoped` (invariant *scoped read-only means no persistent writes*): any spawned reviewer must stay hard read-only — the finalization (tag/commit/push) belongs to the orchestrator, never the reviewer; the lean-dispatch contract must preserve that boundary structurally. Then a spec/build. <!-- id:1968 -->

- [ ] **Extract the directed-relay worktree boilerplate into a CLI tool + shared dep cache** — user request 2026-06-17. A directed/`--afk` `/relay <args>` front session repeats the same bash by hand for every track: `git worktree add ~/.cache/relay/worktrees/<repo>/<track> -b relay/<track> <base>` → `cd … && pnpm install --prefer-offline` (node_modules isn't shared across worktrees) → later, integrate: `git merge --no-ff` → `ckpt-tag.sh` → `git-lock-push.sh --ff-only` → `git worktree remove`/`prune`. Did this ~5× in one session 2026-06-17. Wrap it: `scripts/relay-worktree.sh acquire <repo> <track> [--base main] [--install]` (resolves path + branch name, creates the worktree, provisions deps via a **shared store-dir / XDG dep-cache** so deps are NOT re-downloaded per worktree, optionally takes the `claim.sh` lease) and a teardown/`integrate <repo> <track> -m "<summary>" -l "<model>"` counterpart. COMPOSE the existing `ckpt-tag.sh` / `git-lock-push.sh` / `claim.sh`, don't reimplement. Benefit: fewer hand-typed git calls (each a permission-prompt surface), uniform path/branch conventions, less drift between front-door and pool integrator, no per-worktree ~256MB dep re-downloads. Connects id:1968 + id:8691. (user request 2026-06-17; dep-cache req folded in 2026-06-18 from insights meeting id:f1a7) <!-- id:e79b -->

- [ ] **Pre-scheduled "days-off" → spend the 7-day quota faster on known-idle days (with a reserve floor)** — user request 2026-06-17. The 7-day rolling bucket's whole-window pacing (`RELAY_QUOTA_DECAY_7D` front-loads early, backs off late; `RELAY_QUOTA_THRESHOLD_SEVEN_DAY`/`_SONNET` cap it) assumes the operator might come back any time and want quota left. But the user often KNOWS in advance they won't use Claude Code (e.g. "this weekend I'm away") — on those days the conservative back-off just wastes 7d budget that nobody is competing for. WANTED: a way to **pre-declare idle days/intervals** so during them the pool is allowed to burn the 7d bucket harder (raise the 7d threshold / suppress the decay back-off), while STILL leaving an **adequate reserve** sized to expected usage after the operator returns — never draining to 0 right before they come back. **Design hinge:** the reserve floor is the real parameter — given a known idle interval `[start,end]`, relax the 7d cap *inside* it but keep enough that the window-after-`end` (until the bucket's next reset) still has working budget; the saving is "don't reserve quota for an operator who's provably absent." **Sketch:** a small calendar/intervals source (e.g. `~/.config/relay/days-off.toml` or iCal-ish: `2026-06-20/2026-06-22, reserve=0.20`), read by `quota-stop.sh`'s gate; when `now ∈ an off-interval`, use a relaxed 7d threshold (e.g. burn to `1 - reserve` instead of the decayed cap), reverting automatically outside the interval. **Design qs for a likely `/meeting`:** (a) carrier/format — a TOML intervals file vs a `/relay off <date-range> [--reserve R]` CLI that writes it vs reading the system calendar; (b) how the reserve floor composes with `RELAY_QUOTA_DECAY_7D` (override it inside the interval vs blend) and the 5h bucket (probably untouched — 5h refills fast); (c) per-bucket scope (7d + 7d-Sonnet only) and whether the relaxed cap is absolute or still decays toward the reserve as `end` approaches; (d) auto-expiry + a guard so a stale past-dated off-interval can't silently relax a live run; (e) interaction with the autonomous-campaign id:af30 (the natural consumer — a multi-day unattended campaign over a declared days-off window) and the patient-stop/STOP sentinels (id:d0bc/id:3b1e). Relates to `RELAY_QUOTA_DECAY_7D`, `RELAY_QUOTA_THRESHOLD_SEVEN_DAY[_SONNET]`, `quota-stop.sh`, id:af30 (timed cross-window campaign), id:219b (burnup data to size the reserve empirically). (user request 2026-06-17) <!-- id:2904 -->

- [ ] **Statusline cost should include workflow + subagent token totals (folded in, or a 2nd entry)** — user request 2026-06-17. The Claude Code statusline cost figure appears to count only the main loop, not the tokens spent by spawned `Agent`/Workflow subagents — so a session that fans out many background agents (observed: a directed `/relay --afk` run spawned ~16 background Opus children) badly UNDERcounts true spend. WANTED: the statusline reflects total spend = main loop + all spawned agents + workflows, either (a) folded into the existing `$` cost number, or (b) shown as a second segment (e.g. `$<main> +$<agents>` or `Σ$<total>`). Note the relay already has a live statusline segment (id:15bd: `🔁<round> ✓<done> ⚙<in-flight> Δ$<burn>/h` from RELAY_STATUS.md) and `relay-burn.sh`/`relay-econ.py` already attribute per-agent cost from `profile-run.sh` records — so the data exists; this is about surfacing the AGGREGATE in the always-on statusline, not just during relay runs. Design qs: where the per-agent token usage is readable for the statusline script (agent JSONL transcripts? a running tally file?); main-loop-only vs session-total semantics; how it composes with the existing relay segment so they don't double-count. (user request 2026-06-17) <!-- id:c0bc -->

- [ ] **Per-session cost/token/quota measurement for directed Agent-spawn runs (not just relay-loop workflows)** — surfaced 2026-06-18. `relay-burn.sh`/`relay-econ.py` + the quota-sampling only fire under a relay-loop Workflow (gated on `RELAY_RUN_ID`); a directed `/relay --afk` session that fans out via the **Agent tool** writes NO `quota-samples.jsonl` and isn't captured by `relay-econ.py` (its records come from `profile-run.sh` workflow runs). So a heavy directed session is invisible to the cost/quota tooling. WANTED: a measurement path that works for Agent-spawn sessions. **Reusable recipe proven this session** (works with zero new infra): aggregate `message.usage` (`input_tokens`/`output_tokens`/`cache_read_input_tokens`/`cache_creation_input_tokens` + `message.model`) from (a) each spawned agent's transcript `…/tasks/<id>.output` JSONL **and** (b) the main session JSONL `~/.claude/projects/<proj>/<session-id>.jsonl`; price per-tier (Opus $15/$75 per Mtok in/out, cache-read 0.1×, cache-write 1.25×; Sonnet $3/$15). Wrap as e.g. `scripts/session-cost.sh [session-id]` → per-model table + total + cache-savings line. Pair with id:c0bc (statusline aggregate) — same data source. Also: have a directed run call `relay-burn.sh sample` at start+end so the actual `seven_day`/`seven_day_sonnet` utilization delta IS captured (the only way to get a TRUE % of weekly quota vs an API-$-equivalent estimate). **Seed data point (this session — zkWhale demo-chain, ~20 Opus agents + 1 octopus merge, 2026-06-17/18):** measured **≈ $817 API-equiv** (agents ~$408, main loop ~$409; ~$806 Opus + ~$10 Sonnet); **~395 M tokens processed of which 384 M (97%) was cache-read** at 0.1× — only ~10.5 M fresh, ~1.55 M generated output; **prompt caching saved ~$5 k (~7×** vs no-cache ~$5.8 k); est. **~15–25% of a Max-20× weekly Opus allowance** (≈ 4–6 such sessions/week to drain it). This is the kind of number the tooling should produce automatically. **Per-project breakdown (extension, user request 2026-06-18):** the report must also attribute cost/tokens PER PROJECT/REPO, not just a session total — essential for multi-project sessions like the autonomous `/relay` no-args pool (one run fans agents across many repos). Each spawned agent's repo is knowable from its worktree path (`~/.cache/relay/worktrees/<repo>/<track>`) / cwd / the repo it committed to (and the pool already tags each child with its repo in `relay-events.jsonl` + the claim); group the per-agent `message.usage` by that repo → a per-project cost/token table + the cross-project total. The main-loop (orchestrator) cost is shared overhead — report it as its own line, optionally amortized across the projects it served. Output shape: `session-cost.sh` → per-repo rows + an "orchestrator/shared" row + grand total, so a `/relay` run shows "repo A $X, repo B $Y, … orchestrator $Z". (user request 2026-06-18) <!-- id:6563 -->

- [ ] **Spec (do NOT build) the (C) `relay-pool` sandbox tier** — `--system` unit + ssh-push repo-write model (D5) + file-based push creds; build gated on `af30` authorization. - [ ] [INPUT — meeting] **Write-scope the LLM tier by uid: separate OS users for the relay supervisor/reviewer vs. the executors, so an executor CANNOT write `main` even if it tries** (user 2026-07-17) — the ratified sandbox cluster (id:9d97/b3d0/13ae/02c7/8e7a) scopes only the **mechanical daemon** tier (`relay-ro` discovery producer, `relay-svc` recipe-exec); the **LLM executor** tier is currently unscoped and runs as `tobias` with full write access to every repo's main working tree, refs, and push credential. Proposal: executor uid may write ONLY its own worktree; supervisor/reviewer uid owns `main` + integration. **Motivating instance — VERIFIED 2026-07-17 from the transcript** (`~/.claude/projects/-home-tobias-src-loderite/79ab5449-350a-4a26-9e59-fdb02f2ed3cf.jsonl`, session 11:49, following relay run `relay-20260717-100452-13146`): the agent self-reported *"I initially edited `src/material-field.ts` directly in the main checkout (`/home/tobias/src/loderite`) instead of the worktree"* and flagged it to the integrator. **Threat-model nuance the meeting MUST NOT skip: this was agent ERROR (wrong path), self-caught and self-corrected — NOT adversarial intent and NOT a prompt injection.** So the case for uid-scoping here rests on **error frequency**, not on an attacker model; it is a guard against fat-fingering the canonical tree, which DAC would have made structurally impossible (the agent could not have written it to notice-and-fix in the first place). Do not let the meeting silently upgrade this into an adversarial-containment argument — that argument may also be valid, but it is NOT what this instance evidences. Corollary for cost/benefit: the observed blast radius was ~zero (self-corrected), so the honest question is how often it happens UNcaught. **Evidence base already in hand:** the id:5937 deny-tail probe measured that `permissionMode=auto` denies NOTHING on the executor surface (write-outside-repo, `git push`, network egress all approved) and that **OS-level DAC was the ONLY boundary that actually held** — so this is the one control class with evidence behind it, not a speculative guard (relates id:e2b1/453a — and note `--disallowedTools` is explicitly NOT a boundary, the model routes around it). **Design questions for the meeting — do NOT assume any of these are settled:** (1) git worktrees SHARE the `.git` dir, so file-DAC on main's working tree does not by itself stop `git branch -f main` / a ref write — `refs/heads/main` (and the objects dir the executor must write to commit at all) live in the shared dir; scoping may need ACLs on refs, a per-executor `--separate-git-dir`, or a push-only model. (2) DAC does not stop `git push origin main` — that needs remote-side branch protection or a **credential split** (executor holds no push cred), which is the D5/id:38bf ssh-push model's territory. (3) **This is NOT purely additive: the current executor contract has executors commit AND push** (verified today — the id:521f executor pushed to GitHub + `fievel` itself), so scoping the executor tier REWRITES the contract's integration step; cost is real and belongs in the decision. (4) Interaction with the id:dc5b ledger-collision fix — if executors stop writing shared ledgers at all, dc5b's collision class may partly dissolve structurally rather than need a guard (cf. "prefer dissolving a problem structurally over guarding it"). Relates id:af30 (containment ≠ authorization; this authorizes nothing about the self-relaunching loop shape), id:38bf (the `relay-pool` sandbox tier spec + ssh-push repo-write model — closest sibling, likely merges with this), id:13ae, id:5937, id:d5e0. **CANDIDATE MECHANISM (user 2026-07-17): btrfs CoW-copy each executor's repo and treat executor repos as REAL REMOTES** — i.e. replace the shared-`.git` worktree model with an independent per-executor repo, integrated by an ordinary `git fetch` from the executor's copy. This DISSOLVES design-question (1) structurally rather than guarding it: with its own `refs/heads/main`, an executor writing `main` is *harmless* — it writes its own copy — and uid-scoping collapses to "executor owns its copy, cannot touch the canonical repo" (cf. "prefer dissolving a problem structurally over guarding it"). **Two SEPARABLE claims — do not conflate at the meeting:** (i) *real-remotes topology* is the architectural win and needs NO btrfs (`git clone --local` already yields an independent `.git`; these repos are small — `.git` measured 19M dotclaude-skills / 21M loderite 2026-07-17); (ii) *btrfs reflink as the copy mechanism* earns its place on two specific grounds, NOT raw speed: **(a) `git clone --local` HARDLINKS objects (same inode) = a supervisor↔executor aliasing hazard; `--no-hardlinks` is safe but re-materializes everything — reflink gives independence AND metadata-cost, beating both**; **(b) warm working trees** — a clone checks out COLD (an executor on loderite must `npm install` before vitest can run), whereas `cp --reflink=always -r` copies the whole workspace incl. `node_modules`/`.venv`/build caches at O(metadata), retiring a per-dispatch cost the current worktree model already pays. **Verified 2026-07-17:** `/home` IS btrfs (subvol `@home`, /dev/nvme0n1p2) and `cp --reflink=always` succeeds within `/home` (fails only cross-fs to `/tmp`, tmpfs — expected). **Caveats to carry into the meeting:** `btrfs subvolume snapshot` does NOT work directly — `~/src/<repo>` is a plain dir inside `@home`, not its own subvolume; the cheap path today is reflink-`cp` on plain dirs, UNLESS repos are converted to subvolumes (which additionally buys atomic point-in-time + cheap discard, attractive for parked orphans / id:689c). Copying the whole workspace also copies DIRTY state (executor inherits uncommitted junk) → likely gate on a clean tree. And it COUPLES the relay to btrfs + same-filesystem placement — true on zomni, but `fievel` (Raspbian) likely is not, so a `git clone` fallback is needed if the relay ever runs there. Supersedes nothing; folds into the D5 worktree-per-session model (relates id:d5e0) and may partly dissolve id:dc5b. <!-- id:d03d -->
