Feasible today and partly in use: `agentType` resolves from the `.claude/agents/` registry; `echo-runner` (Tools: Bash) already exists and `relay-loop.js` already pins `discover-shard` to `model:'sonnet'`. **TWO SEPARABLE value props — do NOT conflate:** **(a) BUILD — declarative defaults:** move the scattered imperative `model:`/`effort:` opts in `relay-loop.js` into named agent defs (`relay-execute`→sonnet, `relay-review`/`relay-hard`/`relay-handoff`→opus-apex, `relay-mechanical`→echo-runner/haiku, `discover-shard`→sonnet), so per-subcommand tier/tooling is ONE declarative source instead of imperative sprawl; also shrinks each agent's accidental tool surface. - [ ] **Screenshots of the skills in action + README refresh (root + per-skill) for GitHub** — the public repo is text-only (leads with `CLAUDE.md`; root `README.md` exists but is sparse) and has ZERO visuals, which undersells it for GitHub visitors. Two coupled deliverables: **(1) screenshots/recordings of each skill in action** — captures worth taking: the statusline render (model/ctx%/5h+7d quota/cost/relay segment), a `/meeting` persona round + discoveries output, the relay pool live (`RELAY_STATUS.md` Run-progress + the `🔁<round> ✓<done> ⚙<in-flight>` statusline segment + a `relay-events.jsonl tail -f`), `/projects` dashboard, `/todo-update` + `git-diary` flow, `quota-report.py --spark`. Decide medium: static PNGs (terminal screen-grabs) vs asciinema/svg-term recordings (animated, lighter in git) — lean svg-term/asciinema for terminal flows, PNG for the statusbar. Store under a committed `docs/img/` (or `assets/`); keep them small. **(2) README updates, global + per-skill** — refresh root `README.md` into a real landing page (what the toolkit is, install via `make install`, a one-line-per-skill table, embedded hero screenshots, link to `ARCHITECTURE.md`/`docs/`); update the 3 existing per-skill READMEs (`meeting/`, `git-diary-workflow/`, `todo-update/`) and CREATE missing ones for `relay/`, `projects/`, `meeting-cross/` (currently SKILL.md-only) — each a short user-facing README with its own screenshot + trigger/usage, distinct from the model-facing SKILL.md. Design qs: (a) screenshot medium + where stored + how regenerated (a `make screenshots` helper? or manual); (b) avoid leaking private data in captures (real repo names, quota numbers, paths, tokens — scrub or use a demo fixture); (c) per-skill README vs SKILL.md boundary (README = human/GitHub, SKILL.md = model contract — don't duplicate); (d) keep them from going stale (link, don't copy, the SKILL.md command surface). Scope/sequence: probably a focused docs pass, statusbar + relay + meeting first (highest-signal visuals). <!-- id:daf0 -->

- [ ] **Greppable custom-tool index so sessions find existing helpers before improvising** — user 2026-06-29 (prompted by a NIH session: improvised a `~/src/*` scan + custom toml writer instead of existing relay/scripts; see [[feedback-use-existing-tools-not-improvise]]). A concise machine-greppable index (one line per script: path + purpose, e.g. `relay/scripts/INDEX.md` or a `make list-tools`) would make "before improvising, grep the index" a cheap reflex. **GATE (user):** only build if its consistency with the actual scripts can be **guaranteed** — a hand-maintained index is itself a derived artifact that drifts from source, the exact failure mode of the ledger-derived-index discussion ([[ledger-derived-index-decision-2840]], id:2840) and the "inflownistration" derived-consistency thread. So: auto-GENERATE the index from the scripts (e.g. parse a standard header/usage line out of each `scripts/*.sh`) and/or a test that fails when a script lacks an index entry — never a hand-kept list. Backlog until that guarantee is designed; link, don't build. Relates id:23fe (deterministic scanner), id:2840 (md-SSOT + derived cache, md wins). <!-- id:10a6 -->

When cwd repo == target repo (a single-repo hand-run / --only scope, id:7633) the hazard cannot arise and isolation:worktree is the SAFER tool: it makes the agent's ambient cwd the worktree, so a path slip cannot land in the main checkout. - [ ] [INBOUND routed:c3a3 from loderite hand-run relay-manual-20260717-110236-21] OCTOPUS MERGE TESTED 2026-07-17 AND IT DOES NOT WORK FOR RELAY — supersedes the open question in routed:08eb with an empirical answer. git's octopus strategy does NOT honor custom merge drivers: RELAY_LOG.md is declared 'merge=union' in .gitattributes (git check-attr confirms it ACTIVE), yet 'git merge --no-ff <7ccf> <ba3c>' failed with 'ERROR: content conflict in RELAY_LOG.md / fatal: merge program failed'. Since EVERY relay child appends to RELAY_LOG.md by contract, an octopus merge conflicts on EVERY multi-child wave — the union driver that exists precisely to make append-only ledgers mergeable is silently bypassed by that strategy. Notably ROADMAP.md auto-merged CLEAN (the two children ticked disjoint lines), confirming the routed:c28e disjointness thesis holds; RELAY_LOG.md was the sole blocker. Fell back to serial 'git merge --no-ff' per branch (ort strategy, honors union) — both merged cleanly, zero conflicts. CONCLUSION: keep serial --no-ff as the integrator recipe; octopus buys nothing here and loses per-unit revert granularity. If a future wave-merge is still wanted, it must first solve the union-driver bypass (candidates: pre-merge RELAY_LOG concat, or drop RELAY_LOG from the child contract and have the integrator write it). The failure is FAIL-SAFE — octopus aborted cleanly, main untouched, HEAD intact. <!-- id:b873 -->
- [ ] [INBOUND routed:d6be from loderite hand-run 2026-07-17] MECHANIZE the relay's ROLE boundaries with a pre-commit hook instead of prompt-prose (user 2026-07-17: 'a pre-commit hook that rejects RED-specs (or any test modifications) by non-apex agents, and similarly permits executors to only not modify ROADMAP etc — part of the whole permissions complex and maybe easier than the separate users approach'). TODAY'S EVIDENCE THIS IS NEEDED: the relay enforces every role boundary by PROSE ('do not weaken tests to pass', 'tick only if genuinely green', 'never push', 'work in your worktree') — i.e. pure LLM judgment, exactly what CLAUDE.md's mechanize-first rule says to replace. Observed 2026-07-17 in one session: (a) the ORCHESTRATOR collapsed handoff into execute by telling execute children to author their own RED tests — a self-authored spec proves only that the code does what its author decided; caught by the OWNER, by nothing mechanical; (b) 5 of 6 children edited the MAIN checkout instead of their worktree (the id:c6c8 jobAI incident was an actual COMMIT to a target's real main — a pre-commit hook IN the main checkout rejecting commits whose branch/env marks them a relay child kills that whole class); (c) id:4c84 ticked its ROADMAP box while its function was DEAD CODE. THE TIER SIGNAL ALREADY EXISTS — no new plumbing: the branch name encodes the verdict (relay/<runId>-execute-<id> vs -handoff vs -hard), so the hook can read $(git branch --show-current) and apply per-role rules; belt-and-braces via a RELAY_TIER env var. CANDIDATE RULES: execute ⇒ MAY NOT modify tests/ (the RED spec IS the contract it must satisfy, not edit) and MAY NOT rewrite ROADMAP entries; handoff ⇒ MAY write tests/+ROADMAP, MAY NOT touch src/ (it must not implement); review ⇒ MAY write REVIEW_ME/ledgers, MAY NOT touch src/. ***THE HARD PART — a real counterexample from the SAME session, do not design without it***: id:a78b's ENTIRE JOB was to re-pin a wrong test fixture, because the ROADMAP's own prescription ('re-pin to an octant-masked-cell fixture') was FACTUALLY WRONG (octant cut faces are irregular pentagons + right triangles, never rectangles; only octant CUBE PAIRS give literal squares). The Sonnet executor correctly deviated from the spec, modified tests, and was RIGHT — a blanket 'executors may not touch tests' would have BLOCKED a legitimate correct fix. So the rule needs a deliberate escape hatch (an explicit marker commit? a flag that FORCES a review unit? allow-with-loud-surface rather than reject?) — design it, do not just ban. SIMILARLY the ROADMAP rule cannot be a blanket ban: executor contract rule 2 REQUIRES the child to tick its own box, so the hook needs LINE-SCOPED logic (may flip [ ]→[x] on its OWN id's line; may not rewrite the entry or touch another item's line). WHAT A HOOK CANNOT CATCH (say so up front, do not oversell): id:4c84's spec defect (Acceptance vs Done-check disagreeing — a semantic mismatch); and id:e02a's role-collapse, since apex is MECHANICALLY permitted to do everything and the failure was that it did. VS THE SEPARATE-USERS APPROACH (the user's own framing — 'maybe easier'): agreed it is far lighter (no sudo, no user management, works per-worktree, no ownership churn on shared node_modules/caches) — but name the trade honestly: a hook is BYPASSABLE (git commit --no-verify) so it is guarded by prose again at the last inch, whereas Unix file permissions cannot be talked out of. Hook+prose still strictly beats prose alone, and is reversible; consider it the observe-first step (CLAUDE.md observe-before-preventing) and let the separate-users build be gated on the hook's log showing real firings. Relates id:1735 (self-reported summaries), routed:8adf (isolation:c6c8 rescope), routed:6fd5 (orchestrator self-implementation), the D3 anti-gaming invariant, CLAUDE.md mechanize-first + no-silent-swallow. **CONSOLIDATED 2026-07-19 (meeting `docs/meeting-notes/2026-07-19-1212-git-hook-enforcement-substrate-reconciliation.md`):** this is the **SINGLE relay provenance engine** — id:7a05's provenance-of-tick and id:0c86's executor-no-own-RED detector fold in HERE (one branch/tier read, not three parallel hooks). 077d supplies the L2 role-boundary/provenance checks that **plug into the id:7a05 git-hook framework** (L0 install + L1 dispatch), rather than building its own install path. <!-- id:077d -->
